**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `23:57:20` **dirvine.** said:

The AI part is not compute. It is about giving local access to AI and securing all your conversations and data with it. This will be your AI, we will make it easy to choose, swap models as they become avaliable. The critical part is the local AI and secured only to you conversations. 
Then log into another device and continue securely to add to the conversation. 
This way you are not controlled by central forces and can converse and think freely to maintain YOU'RE control over the AI revolution that is happening and will continue at pace. 
We won't compete with models, we will provide this clear, secure local AI experience to everyone. 
Then RAG/fine tune etc. will also be part of it as your AI becomes more you. 
Later sharing parts of knowledge amongst your friends and so on will happen. 

So think of SAFE AI as all the powers and none of the controls. No humans in between you and it, no contracts between peers and so on. 

SAFE is uniquely positioned to do this and if you go way back to my earlier chats and blog posts you can see this coming. 

When we say AI, think also robots and robotics. These are just knowledge banks like an AI model and likewise must be secured to YOU locally and under only your control. Again no centralised controller or humans between you and it. 

So AI and Robotics is a big play for a truely decentralised network, free of inter peer contracts or centralised controllers. 

I hope with that you can see the unique and vital opportunity we have with SAFE

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1212186742522642543)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `23:26:02` **dirvine.** said:

THe trick here is this. Currently with GPT4 level LLM you can do a lot. An awful lot and industry is showing that, BUT it's centralised. 
OSS models are catching up fast and will overtake GPT4 levels in the coming weeks/months. So then the demonstrations will make a lot of sense. We can demo now with GPT4 but it defeats the purpose. 
So the infrastructure for local AI models is key, securing the conversations and data etc. We can do that now. 

As far as SAFE OS goes, I believe that it may in fact be AI driven.  Why use apps when you can have a local AI model that is secured and knows you, your accounts and so on. You can speak to it and interact like a human. 

So part 1 of the journey in providing this secure enclave for AI / human interaction (and robotics) is critical. If that works AND the OSS models do get to a level they work good enough, then part 2, the SAFE OS is a much much simpler task. 

Of course Agents are a huge part of this and I am working on a mechanism to pre-define agents of all sorts for folk to just gather together to form companies/projects etc.  These will basically be JSON extendable templates in a register. So a CEO register, CTO register etc. 

The good thing is that all of the above is an insignificant amount of work in comparison to a fully fledged app store and OS with all the moving parts it would require.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213628416805310525)

## Sunday, 2024-03-03

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `00:00:19` **dirvine.** said:

@Deleted User Here is something to look at as a simple example. Check alphacode or alphacodium (oss) 
They outperform humans at code competitions. Output judged by humans

The trick is NOT to ask chatgtp to write you a program and expect it works, thats as nuts as phoning a dev and describing what you want over the phone. That does not work, but it's what folk do and report to twitter/mastedon how crappy they are. Of course they are. 

What the likes of alpha codium do (it's agentic like) is take a spec, give it to a dev AI to write code, and other checks the tests and adds more tests, another checks the test match the spec, another refactors and so on. This repeats until the final results is created. 

This is what so many folk get wrong, they think a simple prompt gets the answer, it won't. for tasks requiring steps and  thought processing you need multiple steps and agents to carry them out recursively and iteratively. 

I repeat, it's not a one shot mechanism just like talking to humans to agree an outcome is not a one shot thing. It's a huge error to imagine so and many many folks do just that and report their awful results.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213637045155799060)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:24:32` **Deleted User** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> To be clear. The AI message is to maintain and strengthen those fundimentals in a world where AI exi... [truncated]

By all means tap into the hype and VC network but if Mistral can raise a stack of cash off the back of an investment memo then it's something to consider, the only missing element is having an AI team in place to execute. 
Perhaps identifying key personnel to attract to the project in advance would mitigate this but given the current teams size it would be harder to convince a VC without proof.

Also, it sounds a lot like TBL's original vision for the semantic web, having personal AI agents do a lot of the work for users (aka Web 3.0). LLMs are today's darling but we're already accelerating away from this model so need to consider coming up with our own approach and label for what we want which is akin to federated learning. 

What I'd like more info on is how these personal AI/ agents will operate across devices a user owns if that intelligence is distributed. To enable a personalised AI in a decentralised manner across multiple devices, a distributed file system and a modular neural network structure could be essential. The file system should support fragmenting any AI model into smaller, manageable parts that can be stored and processed on different devices, similar to how blockchain technology fragments data. Federated learning could then be applied, allowing these separate devices to collaboratively learn and improve the AI or agents without sharing the actual data, so maintaining privacy and security that's built as default with MaidSafe. 

Someone else mentioned technical documentation, absolutely critical to have this in place for launch, it's vital to allow anyone to be able to learn how to build not just the existing OSS community. 
"Here's how to build your first MaidSafe app" version of "Hello World" for example. Get kids involved by letting them understand how to code a simple game of Pong that works on the network, or a webpage. These things are vital. It's not enough today to just chuck out release notes and expect non-technical people to "get it".

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213763933945724928)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:41:11` **dirvine.** said:

in SAFE we turn the security on it's head. So instead of secure silo's we say your data may be in fact stored on your worst enemies computer. It's impossible to read etc. but nobody really knows where it is. This security viewpoint makes the Internet security stronger as everything ends up not only encrypted, but information theoretically secure (i.e. there is not enough info in a chunk to decrypt a file or readable information). 

So think of the layers fo security 
Open 
Wan
LAN
AirGapped

and turn them on their head. Then you get the level of security of this network. Open is most secure and LAN or airgapped is least secure (cause we know where you are)

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1215036482859958283)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `22:53:25` **dirvine.** said:

I suspect it's even simpler now. Actors == AI Agents and they can learn. I have some thoughts on specialising them dynamically. What I mean is a colony of agents then require a skill, they create an agent with that skill as it's parameters (system prompt if you like). 
They then grow the colony with this new skill included and on it goes. 

The BIG issue is reward function or "reason for living" type scenarios where we wonder what is the ultimate goal and how can we code it. This is where I think again the answer could not be simpler, but unobvious 
Basically We tell it what we want it to achieve, we add more goals as we go along.  This ties in with SAFE personal AI as we are discussing. We each have our own AI and we give it the current goal. 

This means humanity still has it's innovators, builders and those who cannot be motivated. They all still exist and it's cool.  However those who want to innovate are now super beings with the ability to go from thought -> product/service in seconds and try it out. 

Then ..... then it gets even more interesting.

## Thursday, 2024-03-21

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:45:31` **dirvine.** said:

We did patents way back in 2006-8 to help investors. The story was so crazy that folk thought it was impossible. In Scotland raising cash is a no go basically. I was told software cannot be supported as it can be copied and we cannot take on MS. So a tough situation
I took off to Brno for 9 months. They speak almost no English there. In that time I designed the whole network through patents for each area. 
The patents themsleves though were always available to any small company or project with no fee. They were not available to large corporates (to protect the project). 
Time moved on though and folk now believe in decentralisation, folk even in Scotland invest in software and so on. So we did not need them and basically dumped them. They are not renewed, but were never held to license or prevent innovation (which I hate about patents) 
To see them gone is great. I had a debate with Negraponti (MIT) about patents as in the USA they were not needed quicker than here as investment was more intelligent. 

Thank god though patents are not needed any more and licence lock out hurst society. I am glad they are gone

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1220367692024909908)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:46:20` **dirvine.** said:

I did expect the Engineers at that time to use the patents as design docs. What a fool I was 😄 😄

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:31:55` **rondior** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> We did patents way back in 2006-8 to help investors. The story was so crazy that folk thought it was... [truncated]

It's always amazing to me how a companies perception can shift over time. Whether due to necessity as in this case or just through natural discovery. Even though you encountered significant challenges in the early stages, particularly in terms of securing investment and navigating the landscape of ip, things are starting to come together. Your decision to make these patents freely available to smaller companies while protecting the project from larger corporations was smart and time appropriate. I was actually part of a blockchain project back when Maidsafe was in its early stages, and we faced very similar challenges. We were also working with MIT at the time.

It's great to see attitudes towards decentralization by investors evolve, making patents less crucial. I agree with your thought that patents more than likely will have a negative impact on innovation in this case. This space is never boring and rarely typical.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1220394470546079774)

@Traktion the bootstrap cache shoudl nto have caused the issues you are seeing. That must have been implemented with a bug. I will try and get a look at that soon. It should have made things significantly smoother as nodes and clients would not need to keep asking the same small set of nodes for data and instead use kadmelia properly and ask nodes across the network. 
In addition the cache file is machine wide. So all nodes and clients will use the same file, agian making boostrap etc. much more efficient. 
Sounds like there is a bug implementing that 

I knwo @Bux I had to peek 😄 😄

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `22:31:02` **happybeing** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> It's fine @aatonnomicc I am pulling together a rather large local test rig and have reorganised teh ... [truncated]

Local networks aren't a problem. Even with bugs in Registers they've worked fine and I can do everything with the current build of `awe` on a local network.

Nor are large files the problem I'm seeing on the live network. 

As you know from the issue i filed it is small numbers of small files, to implement simple websites, that the network cannot cope with. @Traktion and others have the same problem, then on top of that all our Eth were used up by being charged for failed uploads with rocketing fees. 

I pointed out the network was a mess months ago and it still is a mess. It gives me no pleasure to be the one pointing this out and getting veiled slights for it rather than solid rebuttals to what I say, but I'm not the only one who sees this.

Meanwhile I continue to build on the basis that it will eventually work, but my confidence in that has never been lower. 

And I don't believe anything that Autonomi promises.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `22:38:16` **dirvine.** said:

rigth now the API uses an in memory only API in self encryoption due to wasm and it's inability to read/write to disk. That also used websockets, which have a network impact that is substancial , that mem only API cannot handle large files. Local network tries to use mdns and sets a 127 ip address (that cannot work as mdns uses multicasting to work). There are lots of small issues like that to be fixed.  i.e. a function to automaticlaly get and bind to a local network interface. I am plouging through them. 
Part of this work is a substancial test suite to run local network that can ttest uoplaod /download of many files of many sizes, plus direcotries etc. That will give us a lot of info of what's workign and not as well as allow us to add tests for any issues folk see.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1322695143056478279)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `22:41:29` **dirvine.** said:

If we get this in place then it becomes much simpler to run local tests. I n addition having bindings for nodejs and pyton allows more devs to get involved. I am using a mkbook impl for a multi language API docs and tutorials that will be part of the repo. That will allow folk to run examples and see what's happening in real time. 

A few weeks ago I promised to make API improvements and I am pushing to make sure that happens. I am not sure how that can be a bad thing in any way.

## Monday, 2024-12-30

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:15:22` **dirvine.** said:

Something I have been very keen on recently and I don't see anyone speaking about it is related. So here's my premise

- Apps also run nodes

So here's the idea.
1. You run a dropbox type app, the running node collects $ to pay for your storage. So there is a delay, but you get apparently "free" lifestime storage of your data. 
2. You run a social media app, the node collects $ and you can comment/like/post etc. So there is a delay again, but ... 
3. You have a local AI and your conversations are stored forever (there's much more to this one, but I will explain when I have a POC) 

Anyway these are examples, but it ties in with a node that "just runs" so a node that collects your right to store. data. Then with mobile apps etc. you read your secret key from a scratchpad and keep going, all while your computer is gathering $$ (when I say that I also mean securing the network) 

Anyway the ability to tightly couple a node to an app coudl prove to be very useful, simple for users and pretty much automatic.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1323278259990954085)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:16:29` **dirvine.** said:

This is why I created the python module for antnode, I hope to publish it again in a day or so and I also hope to create some POC for the above examples.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1323278541445533750)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:04:42` **dirvine.** said:

Pointers can point to anything. So fixed address etc. In combination with LinkedList they can point to head so the LinkedList holds the history if you like. The Pointer can point to head. 

But you can get much more creative as per the docs, so pointer chains and linked list crossover paths and deliberate forks etc. In this way we can handle a lot of use cases

## Thursday, 2025-02-20

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `00:22:59` **dirvine.** said:

I think this quesiton is not well put. It would be more why would you want to store vast amounts of tertirary data on permenent storage. If it's transient then it would be cheaper to use old drives etc. 
Permanent storage is great for most folks data, they want to keep history, but not for transient stuff, like video feeds and what not. 
For public data it has to be perm though as we don't want to lode or have folk change history. 
So in the case of temporary data, I would leave it temporary, but that is a subset of all data really

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341928052376211497)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `00:29:44` **sailingintothewind** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> Yes, I would say it's unlikely to be useful for transient data like that.

ok - If I may, I would like to explain what we do and see what your thoughts are. My clients have 100 computers in marketing suites globally. We sync interactive applications to each of these PCs daily to make sure that they contain up to date marketing material. Daily we receive updates to that data and the old data is removed, new data added. At the moment we use Amazon services to do this. My thought was to see if we could use Autonomi in the future to replace these Amazon services. In order to keep control over our costs we remove old data. Can you tell me what your thoughts are in respect to this use case?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341929748967718962)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `00:39:12` **dirvine.** said:

If it is truly transient then it's likely not worth the costs of perpetual storage, even though perpetual storage on a network like this would be mega cheap in comparison to many services. For you it seems you need a Tb drive locally, but perhaps you would want to keep snapshots over very long periods and that would be fine I would think. They can live happily on autonomi and provide proof points over time. 
There is a mechanism using GraphEntry / Pointer types and scratchpads to handle transient private data though and that may be worth an investigation, but I would think a proof of concenpt woudl be needed. The team are really pushed right now, but in a few weeks or so, I think an example app could show this behaviour if it's intreesting.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341932133429678151)

## Saturday, 2025-02-22

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:56:07` **dirvine.** said:

Some API changes coming in and a fix for the upload Quote issue. That will all help. 
Millions of nodes though is good to see as well. I am interested seeing the results we have now for connection management etc. There has to be some wee adjustments as we go here so all good. 

In terms of is the disk space there, the network does not care. It works like this. 

Rather than trying to have some fancy math and crypto to prove you have space, instead the network ensure you have stored what you should have. So it penalises nodes that cannot provide the data they should have. 

So this is much more like prove by doing as opposed to promise to behave type approach. It's much simpler in many ways but also much less code etc. The proof of storage mechanisms you can employ can be very complex and time consuming. So they work much better in smaller more controlled networks where there is not so much churn and certianly not for small devices. Therefor our approach is consumer first and measure and this allows us to handle much smaller, worse connected and more unstable machines. 

This is the trade off really

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1342857457721933899)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `16:05:15` **dirvine.** said:

A nice debate for a near future is going to be how interoperable we want nodes and clients with the old web. This is also in conjunction with how well do we want AI to access and code with our API and data.  The latter will be very fast and extremely important for every perosn on earth as we collectivly get pulled into a new world, it's up to us to shape how we want that to be. We cannot let it be defined for us by corporates and only a few folks, it must be us and folk like us that define our own future. 

There is a lot of moving parts and we still have to tackle the issue of NAT and routers. i.e. every IOT and computer can connect to the network (Internet or autonomi) but not the other way around. This is a trap we have all fallen into where the large corps etc. say, it's no problem, connect via us. So we need the network to be able to connect TO all devices and that is when we really decentralise. We are getting close, but that battle is not yet won. 

So a ton of interesting and far far reaching advances to be made here, but now we are launched these become rungs on the ladder we are already climbing. 

IF is the start, it's a few seeds we are all sowing together, however we don't proclaim pass or fail with the very first harvest, but we do harvest and then we grow more and then more and we keep going. 

In the background the team need to get the API and all the tech to be as interoperable as possible and give all the magic beans to as many giant killers we can find. Then humanity wins 😉

I don't have strong opinion on what Autonomi should or shouldn't do in terms of apps but they are in a unique position until they get out of the way, by which I mean you I hope have a better understanding of where the network is headed wrt blockchain and reducing or removing the frictions of that, and in the mean time how to best handle that whole area.

It's fair to let the community come up with apps based on the platform and protocol, and the API provides that. What is hard for us to do outside is understand why decisions around the blockchain aspect were made and what they allow as Autonomi go forward.

We were told there would be mitigations for the ERC20 barriers but haven't heard more on that from Autonomi since September, so is that something the community can or should tackle? I wouldn't think so. Similar with native token. I think both those are more API platform like things, and I hope there will be more on both of these as we go forward.

I'm really happy with the projects that folk have put together for IF and some of those have great potential to establish usefulness and bring more people in, but all are stuck behind a big wall called blockchain, so I hope Autonomi have ideas an plans to tear it down!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1372593053835071658)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:28:13` **rid._.dim** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> Hey man, can you see a mechanism for your login session packet (scratchpad) to be universal? I.e. ho... [truncated]

absolutely! that's a pretty smart concept - having one global login to rule them all without the need to even store something in a password database  🎉  without risk of loosing the other keys just because of app glitches that overwrite registered keys in the account package

if we'd derive the app keys (e.g. using the xor-address of the app and/or using clearweb urls for the derivation) that would enable password-recovery from the root without needing to store the derived keys anywhere. On clearnet websites requiring password changes might cause issues but then again the password manager could store (e.g. in a register for permanent storage of that info) a derivation index instead of seed/private key (which is completely useless on its own); certain pages limiting allowed characters could be treated the same way (storing the allowed characters in the register) and having rules how to modify the derived key to just use allowed characters.

using a 2nd factor for device-side security (to secure against keyloggers) like a usb-stick / rfid... / that would either need a service on the device for single-sign-on that can do the derivation for the app(s) or would require the 2nd-factor to be available on every app start.

For full hardware-side external security the external service (based on a typical 12 word derived starting point) would require to be passed the info ("seed" (app), derivation index, and allowed characters) that would be a pretty insane security level but ofc on every input you need to approve on the device then.
If you hook that hardware-password-safe into your Wifi / it gets its own Internet-Connection via mobile Internet even communicating via p2p comms would be on the table for comfort and no need to have wired/bluetooth connections.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:40:36` **jamesstaff_** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> James, do you see a futue where all your records belong to you and each medical practice gets access... [truncated]

Hey David, 
Thanks for the great insight.

Medical Records Ownership: The quick answer is yes; the longer answer is there is a lot of complexity. For example, in the UK, the NHS or healthcare provider that created and manages your medical records is the legal owner, not the patient (!) however you are legally entitled to access them. With time we plan to build in this guidance based on user location e.g. if you are in the UK you can quote law XYZ to get access if refused initially. Due to this our initial target market is Global Citizens & Digital Nomads (and with time displaced populations) so those looking to cross borders and bring their records with them as we see these as "lower hanging fruit" & more tech forward individuals. We plan to have translation as default so you can share records to providers in whatever language is required & translate reports you receive e.g. the MRI Results I received on my back were in Portuguese so I had to translate

General Vault System: In parallel to Health, we are planning to develop smart vaults for other critical documents. On a call yesterday with a mentor he jumped directly to using vaults for his Will, we will build a smart tagging system for core documents (house deeds, wills etc.) with access granted to different groups / under conditions

Sharing: Exactly as you outline, the individual would share the records and this could be on a timestamp e.g. you share your SOMA ID to somebody who needs your name, DOB & Password but the link expires after 1 hour, or it could be a long term share but you can revoke the rights. This is why we plan to have SOMA Companion for individuals & SOMA Colleague for healthcare providers so long term a complete health ecosystem with the individual controlling who has access. We are currently working with @zettawatt  to utilize Colony as the backend infrastructure 

Complexity: Under no illusions on this. We are actively recruiting advisory board members arounds key areas (legal, policy, medical, technical) to ensure what we are building comes from a well-informed place. It's also our reason for aiming at Global Citizens & Digital Nomads as the NHS (for example) is potentially a long-term aim but we need to first build up a user base. If there is anybody in the community / your network, you think would be interested in these intros are welcome. 

Hugging Face: Thanks for sharing, @connie had previously been looking at this & agree it could be a great resource

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1372886450873434123)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:43:19` **happybeing** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> Perfect @riddim This all adds so much strength to the app and takes it well beyond what you were doi... [truncated]

I outlined a scheme for using named keys. tl;dr:

You have a master secret key and can derive named keys based on that. Your master key unlocks a Vault which contains a list of each named key you have. An app such as dweb-cli is shown the master key and can access and update that list.

Any app using dweb REST API tells it which key to use based on what the user asks for. So I tell my Friends app to use my the "social" key or the "Friends" key or "default" etc. Friends never sees the secret, it just includes the key name in any REST calls that mutate data.

This model could I expect fit into or be used to specify something like you mentioned David but I am busy so not implementing it yet.
cc @riddim

EDIT: At the moment dweb derives a key based on an app ID supplied by the app and the SECRET_KEY, so the naming isn't used yet and isn't needed for dweb apps. Only if we broaden this out to more apps which don't used an app id in this way themselves. This keeps each app's data in a separate name space. I have simiar key derivation for each data type, and names for each object on top of that.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1372887131164381265)

## Tuesday, 2025-06-03

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:23:04` **dirvine.** said:

To be clear, we cannot guarantee there will be no earth ending events etc. but the design is data perminance. So there is nothing in the design to delete or lose data. 
That's the only guarantee we can make really. 
I dislike hearing guarantees as there is never such a thing in this crazy universe, however the intent and design are things that can be measured. In terms of how they work and how valid those statements are then, like everything, the longer they appear to hold true the more confidence folk get that it is true, but nobody should ever realy consider anything that is measurably true today will also be tomorrow 🙂 

An interesting find from back in the gnutella days (early p2p) was that a node online for X hours is likely (over 50% probability) to be online for 2X Hours. 

So that's a consideration, but guarantees of anything are kinda like Tesla windscreen is guranteed to withstand a nuclear blast 😄 It's kinda the same joke in reality

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1379389920778653767)

## Tuesday, 2025-06-10

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:06:59` **dirvine.** said:

I think the issue would be you could consider all current private keys know. So history could be preserved but all existing wallets invalid. 
The key will be move to lattice or similar and everyone needs to create new wallets and move on. The history though can be preserved as this happens which is important. However rewriting the blockchain will still be non trivial as it’s hashes and not modulo arithmetic issues. The latter being trivial for quantum but the former I think is largely unaffected as of now at least

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:56:47` **curiousweb** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> I think the issue would be you could consider all current private keys know. So history could be pre... [truncated]

Thanks for your reply. Maybe I'm mistaken, but it sounds like you're maybe conflating wallet security (private key protection) with what I was meaning about blockchain integrity (historical consensus verification). I was thinking more about being able to detect inconsistencies between live Bitcoin nodes and archived snapshots. Moving Bitcoin to Lattice or similar would be completely replacing Bitcoin's cryptographic foundation with quantum-resistant mathematics. If they did such a migration then even then, wouldn't such a quantum secure history in Autonomi provide a way to independently verify the legitimate pre-quantum state of Bitcoin during such a massive cryptographic transition, thus doubly ensuring that the new quantum-resistant Bitcoin launches with a quantum secure verifiable historical foundation, rather than a potentially compromised version?   I understand such a quantum hack would be nigh impossible anyway, but again was thinking more of the complementary nature of Autonomi in helping other such networks address such risks often touted in the media to sow FUD, however remote.

Or to summarize - you could maybe think of the idea as a quantum-secure "blockchain health monitor" 🙂

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1381995516686237696)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:30:15` **dirvine.** said:

@riddim iroh like libp2p would give some centralisation, but we AVOID that in BOTH. Here's how. The centralised parts are relay servers and STUN servers. For us these can be part of a node as currently we do with relay. So we avoid ANY centralisation. So that's not a worry with iroh or liibp2p for us. 

In addition to this Quinn needs an update but the IETF have put forward a QUIC draft for NAT traversal without STUN, so there is a likelyhood we can use QUIC extentions for NAT traversal and not then even need iroh or libpp2.  These IETF agreements are extremely welcomed and we have waited 5 years on this news. You can read about it here https://www.ietf.org/archive/id/draft-seemann-quic-nat-traversal-01.html

This also links to the other centralisation issue of "cold start" i.e. you need servers to bootstrap from, but what if there was a new way to tell folk over the phone or in quick text message who to connct to and then they collect addresses (this collection is what our bootstrap_cache does and that is important). So to get over this codl start and ability for folk to share netwkring endpoints (horrifically complex things, esepcially with ipv6) So the cold start without any centralisation is vital. 

So what if we had a mechanism where 3 english words is all you need to connect to the network. 3 wrods where anyone can share them over the phone and so on, so look here https://github.com/dirvine/three-word-networking where we cna do exactly that (6 words for ipv6).

To get there, we need our internal KAD impl, thorough testing and a network abstraciton layer. Then we can progress to a massively capable NAT traversal, close to 100% connectivity and in a way we have address hand off, relay handoff (never relay actual data, but connections)  and all with way way less code and way way more capabilities wiht data xfer at maximum possible speed with the highest possible levels of security. 

Then TLS 1.3 etc. with ed25519 or older tls 1.2 with more round trips (4 instead of 3) and quantum security issues, which are real, but we have quantum secured data underneath, then we are quantum protected in our lightweight, secure and minimal fully connected network. 

It's a lot of moving parts and much of it will be lost on many folk and almsot all of it will be invisible if we do it right, but it gets us where we want to be. 

Privacy Security and Freedom for every person on the planet in this digital world 😉

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:42:00` **dirvine.** said:

The fascinating thing is the sizeof the networks that evolve to produce these results. They are tiny. So math is really not real, it's created by us and unnatural, but ot follows rules, almsot logical, so we can test an AI output for correctness and train it. So here we start off small and evolve the network to a size it knows it can do arithmetic, or calculus (wee bit bigger) and it gets amazing results. 

It's unclear why and no AI or person I have spoken to knows why, but they are a bit dumfounded. I am just very curious and cannot get it into my head quite yet, but it's very very fascinating when we evolve to an answer rather than activate a massive set of neurons each time. 

It's like growing intellignce instead fo encoding it. HEre we don't train on data, we evolve the right size and shape of "brain". So it's kinda mental. 

It was a fun few weekends doing that one

1. Current Security Architecture Review

1.1 Multi-Layered Defense Model

Our existing P2P Foundation implements a sophisticated defense-in-depth security model:

┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│            Application Layer            │ ← MCP Auth, Permissions
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│             Protocol Security           │ ← Message Integrity, Encryption  
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│              DHT Security              │ ← S/Kademlia, IPv6 Diversity
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│            Transport Security           │ ← QUIC/TLS 1.3, Certificate Validation
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│            Network Security             │ ← IPv6 Tunneling, NAT Traversal
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘
1.2 Quantum-Resistant Cryptography

Current Implementation (FIPS 203/204 Compliant):

Key Encapsulation: ML-KEM-768 (192-bit classical, 128-bit quantum security)
Digital Signatures: ML-DSA-65 (192-bit classical, 128-bit quantum security)
Threshold Signatures: FROST-ed25519 for t-of-n signing
Symmetric Crypto: AES-256-GCM with HKDF-SHA256



Truncated

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:56:51` **dirvine.** said:

Privacy in blockchain transactions is a well studied thing, same with (pseudo) anonymity, lots of scaremongering and false claims. 

However on the network the data stored is only known to the node(s) storing it and the blockchain transaction cannot decypher what was stored for what payment. It's a hash, so one way and secure. 

The privacy details are much deeper, but the basics are the blockchain payments are no more revealing to users than the native token DAG was, almost  the same except the native token DAG DID tie data to payments. So in that way our blockchain impl is more private. 

As I say though, privacy security and anonymity are very long subjects, but that is the basics.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1391885700789436558)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:59:22` **dirvine.** said:

In both systems node to node or client messages are TLS secured, so not able to be snooped on by any normal person or org (state actors aside as there will always be a question mark there)

> *dirvine. said:*
> I got cut off, but folks that are here for the money will absolutely do that very well with ANT, nat... [truncated]

Getting the network stable & working well is of course the top priority; with out that there's nothing to build on. 

But economics is also important in determining how things go with the network.

Native ANT may not make ANT holders more money than ERC20 ANT, but it would very likely reduce the cost of access to Autonomi's services for the wee lass in the bush.

If native halved the cost of uploading to Autonomi long term it would benefit many people, and influence how people use the network.

If it's a distraction for the team it should absolutely stay on the back burner until the time is right, but how much it costs to use Autonomi seems like a pretty important thing that should be ok to discuss without being thought of as caring only about money.

So, not on the blockchain, but there's some logging around it, that seems unnecessary and a possible source for trouble.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:59:12` **getafoxcom55226** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> I think you are confusing data and money really. The money part, yes we cannot right now do a monero... [truncated]

You have a utility token but it is impractical to use it because the integration with the blockchain multiplies the transaction costs involved in storing data on the network.  In order to reduce the transaction cost for someone to acquire the utility token (pay 1 gas fee to convert ETH to ANT) you have multiplied the transaction costs of actually using the network (pay up to a max of 1 gas fee per chunk if you are super unlucky).  It would have been better keep the network a closed system.  I can always find someone who wants to sell me some of the token on facebook marketplace and we can arrange our own transaction and payment details. I would like to use the network for its primary purpose - securely storing my data - but I cannot because its just going to be too expensive, and needlessly so.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:28:04` **dirvine.** said:

No worries @PaulthePotter it's not always easy and when the answers off the top of the screen then folk turn it around. You can scroll up, but blockchains are not anonymous, no matter what anyone says. However in our case teh transaction does not expose any data name or location etc. So the data is not on the blockchain in name or metadata etc. 

In terms of L1 L2 ligntneing and all the other currencies, I think that's just a wider version of vim/emacs fights. I don't get involved there at all, so many opinions. 

In terms of the gas fess, now they can be paid in ANT as well. So the overall cost is £X We don't know if a native token would be cheaper or not. The network tries to balance supply and demand. So when there is a lot of data then it's likely storage will cost what node runners are happy to accept, regardless of fees. So the fees do get in the way but maybe not s much as we think, but I don't know. I realy want to be focussed on the network itself and the folks buildign on it as they will bring the value.

So fees are like a tax but not the end of the world jsut yet, with the supply/demand thing (node runners for instance will only have a small fee for hopefully a large transfer when they cash in).  So it MIGHT not be as bad as we think there. The bigger portion of the tax is in uploads and right now with ANT at such low low costs that tax seems large, btu again if ANT does what we want then that tax may not seem as bad. 

Then who knows what will happen, but to get there we really need to get focussed on utility and value in the network itself.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:35:51` **dirvine.** said:

No @PaulthePotter but there is a ton of ways to expose many things. These days we have backdoored hardware, operating system and more. So great care is required. But no the network does not log such things. Individual nodes you pay will see the payment and the data. So there is that, but there always has to be that. However they cannot tell what of your chunks belong to what files and  so on. 

Security like this is a massive massive field with infinite questions, the basics are the payments don't link data to files and they don't link files to blockchains and so on. 

You can download a BAD app and it will just steal all your wallets and data though, so that side needs also great care.

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:39:39` **dirvine.** said:

Think of chunks as information theoretically secured clumps of bytes. They physically cannto be decrypted by any form of computation. They do not link to each other or identify a file. Without the data map they are perfectly harmless for infinite time. 

information theoretically secured  -> means the chunk does not physically contain the data you require to decrypt it.

## Sunday, 2025-07-13

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:57:58` **dirvine.** said:

I think there is confusion here. I hope I can help. 
So maidsafe (autonomi) is an answer to the big corporates who control the internet via everything going through their servers and of course having to authenticate with them. 

So the network allows peer to peer networking and cloud like services (real cloud not just another server farm).  This is a mix of p2p services and individual sovereignty.  So this is not a p2p ONLY network, no such thing can truly exist (yet, but many are working on this part) as it currently IMPOSSIBLE to p2p connect 100% of computers. So this is a mix of individuals computers hosting services for us all, they do not know what they are hosting and cannot see what they are hosting (due to highly encrypted data chunks that are unreadable with any kind of computer or quantum computer etc. so actually impossible to read),

Therefor the network is designed in a way to connect a many computers together as to provide the services we all need. To achieve that node runners get paid in ANT from people who just use it or cannot themselves run nodes. 

So whether anonymous autonomous p2p etc. is used to describe it and equally to criticise it, the above is the actual design and reason for the design. 

I am not criticising or defending any angle here, just clarifying the design and real world capabilities of not only this network, but of todays technology.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1393999912579891210)

Things seem to be settling after the main net upgrade. Stick with it folks, we jsut went round a corner fast there, stabilising now,

## Monday, 2025-07-28

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `08:08:16` **dirvine.** said:

That means somebody coded scratchpads to update but did not update the counter. So created them wrong. Each updated content must update the counter or you break CRDT rules. Perhaps our docs are not clear on that, but scratchpads and poiners are not high concurrency devices and they cannot be multiuser updated, they need single owners updating them and updating the counter and in case of concurrent uploads with same counter then the user must decide on what path to take and give a new one with the counter updated again. 

If they are allowed multi access and multi update with zero co-ordination then you will get this situation and its perfectly correct. 

Again our docs should make this clear, perhaps they don't?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1399287329574883370)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `08:10:57` **dirvine.** said:

This is why these types are owner signed and only the owner should have teh secret key to do that

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1399288003876093952)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `10:44:51` **dirvine.** said:

That is possible for sure. If you had a client for instance that updated a pointer/scratchpad then somehow forgot that info (restart or whatever reason) and then read the latest and got an old one through bad luck and also updated that to the new version, causing a conflict with the previous update, then yes that can happen. 

It's unlikely (unless there is a bug) the network would not replicate these in time, but it is of course possible to get into the situation you describe. To not do that, if the client remembered it's current state and updated from there, it would certianly help.

I mean:
- sometimes it works as expected: typically I create a Pointer with one target and then immediately update it so it takes a new target and the count is incremented. Later I update it, and later update it again. I've seen this work for more than ten updates and I believe @Josh  managed 40-50 (with dweb publishing Atlas) a while back.

I can repeat the update and it always remains with the first count and target. This was happening quite frequently a few weeks ago.
- at other times it has worked as expected for a while, but after a week or two won't update further (but no errors thrown). 
- another behaviour which may no longer happen (I'm not sure because now I generally see 'stuck' pointers and can't update them), at least in the past was that after a number of updates, I would get different 'versions' of the pointer returned with different gets. This may have been fixed, not sure.
- yesterday I was getting record does not exist errors for a pointer I created a couple of months ago. But I only tried once as I don't have much time for this atm.

## Tuesday, 2025-07-29

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:16:08` **dirvine.** said:

Getting rid of relay right now for nodes is a solid move. I have been crying for it for a while, the team were not pushing for this and we did have debates on decentralisaiton. However this is a red herring in my opinion
Decentralisation does not mean 100% of people can run a node from 100% of homes. Decentralisation means that there is no middleman between you and your data, or you and your app, or your app and your data. That is exactly what we're doing here. 

Thinking that losing 1% of the current network is us being a traitor or whatever to decentralisation isn't valid. It's us making the network more stable and secure, which is exactly what we have to do. 

And of course, we are working very hard in the background—the same as any peer-to-peer project—trying to get to as many computers as possible and homes as possible. That is not an easy task. It's never been done. There's not enough IP4 addresses. IP6 isn't taken up very well. Routers and the way they work don't allow incoming connections very easily.

That works for the incumbents; it works for the corporations; it works for the governments. It harms peer-to-peer networking. 

So that is the reality. We are working on it. 

We're working on it quite hard. I've got a side project looking at some very leading edge nat traversal technology to help here. It's not ready for our network yet. It's not ready for probably production yet. 

But there's a lot of work happening in the background, but we need to have an awful lot of focus on the user experience of this network. Can you pick up an app? Can you run it? Can you protect your data? Can you securely speak to other people you want to speak to? Can you securely store data?

These are all things that are much more important, and things we have to work on. 

So it's brilliant that we're all so motivated to really push for security and privacy and the right to our own data—and it's brilliant that we're all on that same road. We just need to face the same direction and realise if there's a river we have to swim over it, if there's a bridge we have to walk over it. There are lots and lots of things in our way. There will be, but we have to keep moving and keep moving forward.

We can't release 100% of the technology that's going to last forever. This will always evolve. What we can do is put out the best we can, when we can, given the resources we've got. One of our biggest resources is our community, and that's vital for our success. So with a strong community and a solid team working, it might not be the largest team in the world, but it's a solid team and they're all working hard.

We make progress. How fast that progress is, how perfect that progress is—is difficult to say, but we work hard and we make progress—and that's what's important.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1399847988511117322)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `22:26:20` **dirvine.** said:

It is a network for everyone. Right now, it's currently technically impossible for every person to run a node from home— currently technically impossible—but we're working on it.

This is a network for everyone, but "everyone" means everyone can use it. It doesn't mean everyone can run a node from home. As many people as possible will, and we'll continue to expand that.

We have taken numerous technical hurdles, which are currently not possible. We'd go one step at a time. But moving one step at a time means exactly that. We have not released 100% of privacy, security and freedom for every person on the planet yet, but surely working towards that makes perfect sense. I don't know how else to say that. People could say we've deviated because we haven't released everything, but all that we can do is keep moving forward—adjusting our position and heading there. However, if as a company certain things would become illegal for us to do, we cannot as a company do those things.

It doesn't mean those things won't happen in some other way, but as a company MaidSafe would not be able to do something which was against the law and where one of the directors would have to go to prison for it. I don't think anybody wants that.

So forward, sensible progress towards the original vision surely is a fantastic way to work.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:39:27` **dirvine.** said:

At the moment it's much more about what is feasible as opposed to fair. I don't think it's fair personally that IPv4 and NAT restrictions prevent people from having nodes they can connect directly. 

I totally agree where you've got computer-to-computer communications relaying—might be necessary, but we have to recognise that you're relaying through a third party. If that's not one of your friends, or if there's another way to expose you, then that's also problematic. 

Direct connecting is definitely the way forward, and I think that's something we want to really try and get to.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1400065248857296928)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:41:08` **dirvine.** said:

The whole idea with Impossible Futures is they will show us things that we didn't see—that's really the key: let people's imagination lead the way. There will be lots of people who say "you must have x" and "you must have y," but in all honesty, when the internet started nobody knew about Uber and nobody knew about Google.

Things have to evolve. The best way for us—or our approach—is to let as much as possible evolve as easily as possible. Don't make any demands on people and let's see what the crazy ideas produce.

It's all about the crazy ones in my mind. It's the people who are going to do things that we couldn't have imagined—and that's exactly the platform that Impossible Futures should provide and hopefully will provide.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1400065675266883584)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `16:40:20` **dirvine.** said:

There's no real feasible way of doing that—and we don't trust other nodes to confirm it. Also, somebody could have 35 gig at a test and then—when the test finished—remove the 35 gig. It's a bit of a tricky situation.

Instead, what we do is penalise nodes when they don't have data that they're supposed to have. That's the best way that we've found so far, anyway.

Rather than promising to have the space (or temporarily having the space), we actually focus on: did you have the data that you were supposed to have?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1400140970120445972)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `16:42:32` **b_dazz** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> There's no real feasible way of doing that—and we don't trust other nodes to confirm it. Also, someb... [truncated]

Could you elaborate on what the penalties consist of?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1400141522791436443)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `16:51:55` **dirvine.** said:

Penalties in this network basically mean all other nodes that are finding bad behaviour ignore you, don't add you to the routing table—so as a node, you become invisible basically. 

The issue with doing the check—it's like: who does the check, who's got the authority to say that check is correct, and what does it actually mean if it was correct at that one point in time? 

Because anybody could write a script that says "I'm doing an upgrade" or "clear out space, show space and then put my data back"—or whatever. People do all sorts of things to get past any kind of check, so bad behaviour probably is just going to happen. 

Our approach is just to detect actual bad behaviour—behaviour that harms the network—and ignore those nodes, keep them out.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1400143882578034770)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `16:52:19` **dirvine.** said:

Bad behaviour and how we react to bad behaviours are really, really interesting, and it gets pretty deep pretty quick, but it's a very interesting thing to look at in a permissionless peer-to-peer network.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1400143985649123339)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:44:29` **dirvine.** said:

It's my opinion that if you look at open source projects, open source maintainers always have an absolutely terrible time. When you introduce money into the situation, that makes it even worse. If there's a company involved—regardless of how that company's been configured, where it's maybe not even taken VC money (that's irrelevant)—it's a company, so people will attack it. 
And ultimately, if people are not aligned, I don't think we can force alignment. That's my personal opinion. The more open you are, the more open you are to FUD. Then you have people that just want to criticise, they want to claim that promises are broken and named their first child after you—some sort of crazy stuff. Just loads and loads and loads of people behind fake names, making fake claims about fake things. That's just the way life goes. 
So ultimately, there's not really much you can do about it, but I think personally, I try and ignore it. I prefer this place here because it's a quick conversation. 

Hopefully it's light-hearted conversation where there's some information provided—and every so often there's an AMA or some sort of presentation. There's a Stages event, there's a news channel to try and let folk know what's going on in the bigger sense. We've got a general support channel to help people, the Impossible Futures channel to try and help those teams. But ultimately, at the end of the day, we've got to build the product. We've got to do the hard slog and the hard miles behind the scenes. But that involves fairly deep, long, thought-out conversations. People prefer talking about things like tokens or whatever because there's not an awful lot involved there. 

Everybody can have a different opinion and they can all be correct. You can have knee-jerk responses. You can have knee-jerk, fairly intelligent sounding criticism. But ultimately, behind the scenes, there's some deep, deep, deep thinking that has to happen, and the team has to be involved in some of that deep thinking. So folk will demand that the team answer every question or whatever. But we are in 2-3 hour meetings during the day. There's teams meeting up, doing video conferences during the day. There's lots and lots and lots of work back and forth. 

We do try and communicate with the community, but we can't communicate on every request. The actual community Forum is not a healthy place at the moment for anyone's mental health. It actually concerns me a bit—even the people that are on the Forum are maybe damaging their own mental health by screaming, shouting, kicking, spitting, and swearing. But hopefully here, with the fast conversations—maybe a little bit more pleasant—it's just that little bit easier. You have to communicate. But even so, there'll be the odd person every so often saying, David, you said this, or David, you're doing that, or David, you're whatever. But here, it's a lot easier to ignore that kind of thing.

And my own personal belief is you either know yourself or you don't know yourself. And that's up to each individual. Anyway, I wouldn't get too upset or too worried about the extreme people. It's just like being in the street.

You don't need to answer the drunken alcoholic with slevers falling out of his mouth and blood and guts everywhere. You can just walk on past. And honestly, you're better just walking on by most of the time. Apart from that, it's all great fun.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1404883255924228259)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `07:14:24` **dirvine.** said:

Here is a wee utility called sb (saorsa browser). As we enter the agentic coding days with claude code, cursor-agent, openai cli, gemini-cli, qwen-cli etc. then you have these agents do code/docs etc. but often you don't see all they produce, so you get vscode/vim etc. to help you and then you are distracted (not so much with vim).

So this wee utility is a cli and shows you your markdown or code files in preview mode (i.e. rendered) and also allows delete/move etc. as well. You can press "e" and edit any file in real time and so on. 

Think of this as a cli tool that allows you to quickly track the work, check the work and get to grips with the docs as your agents work away in the background. 

https://github.com/dirvine/sb/blob/main/README.md

If you have rust installed then `cargo install sb` will do it for you. then in any dir just type `sb` and you have a view of your code and docs 

The intention is a new cli browser for a markdown only web as we move forward, but that is a side qwest for now.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1405071979647860787)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:00:40` **dirvine.** said:

It's all about specification, design document, up-to-date documentation. The code has really little to do with it.

You have to document everything, document clearly your expectation, do test plans, test-driven development, have agents that run your tests, agents that write your tests, agents that write your code, code review agents, documentation agents. So it's a much larger job than writing code. The code writing part of it is really quite tiny. 

If you imagine it's like managing a team of autistic savants in terms of the code, they'll do exactly what you ask them, given the context that you give them. 

If your code base is evolving and you're not evolving your documentation with it, then that's maybe something only humans can handle. But if you evolve your documentation along with the code base and have extremely detailed, thought-out plans for what you're going to do next—it works exceptionally well. Way, way, way, way better than a human.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1405128918016458883)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:02:38` **dirvine.** said:

What I should say is: if anyone picks up an AI tool and just types prompts into it, they're going to have a terrible experience—unless they're just doing toy apps or the kind of apps you're describing (the kind of vibe coding type thing). For decent size code bases, it's all about becoming a manager of a team that will do exactly what you tell them.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1405129416119554050)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:04:32` **dirvine.** said:

The side projects I'm working on, I would probably not let a human interfere with the code or interact with it because I don't think they would update the documentation and the tests as well as the AI does.

So I think if you get humans interfering with that process, you have to put another process in place to then capture all the changes—which is fine because the AI can look at the Git log. If the human has put decent commit messages to explain the thought process, why they were doing the change, what they hoped to accomplish, and the results of the test to prove what they accomplished, that might be okay.

But humans tend not to do that part, whereas I can make the AI do that part.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:07:12` **dirvine.** said:

I use Claude code quite a bit, and I've got quite a significant setup there with various commands that I've written, as well as hooks and agents. I also use qwen-cli, Cursor Agent, as well as OpenAI CLI tool, so I use quite a mixture. I tend to rely heavily on tight specifications, design documents and different agents to write code, test code, check the security of code, write tests, run tests, etc. So they all work independently and they should check each other's code. On top of that, I'll run many of the different things like Qwen, OpenAi, and get them to evaluate how well the specification has been met by the other AI. 

So quite a bit of back and forth with various AIs. Unfortunately, I don't think there's really a shortcut. I think it comes down to what would be your management style—if you had very capable programmers, designers, testers, DevOps people that will do exactly what you say. That really reflects a lot in how well you write the specification. 

For instance, I also use MCP servers, so I've got a DigitalOcean MCP, a GitHub MCP, Docker MCP—so I can do things like: just tell my AI, "Set up Docker instances in five discrete geographies, start nodes on each of them, give me a latency report for those nodes and watch the cost." 

At the same time, we committed code to GitHub and telling the GitHub agent to watch the workflows, make sure everything's up to date, check the security analysis. If there's any issues with workflow: let's pull it down, write a specification for a fix, we'll agree the fix and then move forward.

The Docker guy—sometimes I'm speaking to him—and creating a whole bunch of Docker images to create a mini network on the local machine or even push that through the DigitalOcean MCP to lots of other machines. 

It's quite an involved process, really. I think it really comes down to leaning very heavily on AIs themselves. Here's what I want to do, how would you do it given my configuration, and how can we improve the configuration slightly, keep improving the config until you get to a place where you're quite happy. For instance, my Claude code would be my main thing, and it could be working on something for an hour, but it's connected also to 11 labs.

When it's finished with some agentic work, it'll alert me (it'll say to me, "David, this is finished, what do you want to do next?"). Then I can walk over to the computer, have a look at what's done, and work out the next steps—but do so in a really focused way. So you're not sitting, staring at a screen the whole time. You're away thinking about things, reading the specification documents—and there's quite a lot of work to it. But for small stuff, you can just grab any of those AI agents and do the vibe coding thing, but it just doesn't do anything for me.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1405160763659784272)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:32:50` **dirvine.** said:

I tend to start with a lot of research, use a lot of AIs with source documentation, read docs, etc. The initial specification for any project I'm doing takes quite a while. So it's really ideation. There's a lot of that—lot of conversations with different AIs, looking at what's been done before, and if we can pull things together to make something new.

Also, spending a lot of time with the IETF documents and papers and research papers to see what's coming. Even on occasion, I'll do things like give an AI a research paper, get it to extract code from it, write a programme, and show me exactly what it means and what the impact would be, etc. Then ultimately solidify the idea, pull that into a specification that would get us stage one of whatever it is I'm trying to build, and then really iterate on that.

A lot of the docs that I do, though, are a user story type mechanism to progress things in a way that makes sense from a product perspective.

## Wednesday, 2025-08-20

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:05:50` **dirvine.** said:

Using the timestamp probably is helping you here to make sure you're always setting the latest counter. However, I would say that something is setting the counter, and it must have your private key to sign the packets with the counter. So, something in the app is not syncing, it's not getting the latest update, and it's not remembering its own latest counter. There's something a bit weird in the app synchronization there. I would say as well. It might be worthwhile if you're doing that kind of thing that you do keep the last update that you did and then update again. 
However, I think using the Unix timestamp is probably the smartest way.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `23:06:23` **zettawatt1** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> Using the timestamp probably is helping you here to make sure you're always setting the latest count... [truncated]

It doesn't have very often anymore, it was mostly when the network was having trouble a couple weeks back. Since I can have multiple client applications, I can't trust the current count value, I always have to fetch to get the latest count value. So say I do an update to a scratchpad. I fetch the scratchpad, get the count, and upload the new contents/count to the network. I hop on another instance of colony some time later, perform the same steps, but sometimes I don't get the latest scratchpad, I get the previous one. So I push up this new scratchpad, only now I've got a conflicting count value. The network either accepts it based on whatever peers I'm connected to and I get the forked scratchpad error on the next fetch, or it is rejected because the count is the same as what's already there. If I was tied to one device I wouldn't have to worry about it and just use the local cache's count for that scratchpad, but I'm fully reliant on the network for syncrhonization, so I've got this issue. From a user standpoint this may never happen, but I'm stress testing to find bugs so I get more of these fun corner cases 😆

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1407848268708446228)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:40:25` **dirvine.** said:

I think there's some confusion with CRDT-type applications. 
So if you've just got purely random data that doesn't depend on the data prior to it, then setting the Unix timestamp type probably is fine. 
But if you've got actual data that you're trying to use in a CRDT, then that wouldn't be good because you would be potentially ignoring the latest commit to that piece of data.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1408098424431054949)

I honestly think that potentially scratch pads (because they can contain any data) are just being used as a way to bypass all data types and do any kind of application you want, but ignoring concurrency issues that may happen if you do that.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1408101731182706689)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:55:12` **dirvine.** said:

This is the crdt thing @Traktion what should be happening is all nodes, i.e. actual network nodes and clients should be updating and merging changes continually. So the quorum issue and how it works breaks this pattern a bit. 

What we need to do is have clients who receive differing version, update all nodes they know of with the latest version and same for nodes, if they ever (via replicaiton etc.) see each other with older data, they must update it. 

This should be the case for pointers and scratchpads

So we do have a bug here, but also I think differing uses of the CRDT pattern

cc @QiMa

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `16:06:01` **dirvine.** said:

I suspect the quorum might be causing issues with both pointers and scratch pads. If one node has got the latest copy of a pointer or scratchpad, but no others have it, it won't meet that quorum figure. It won't be returned to the user, which is mental. 

This is a definite bug that could and would give us issues with both of those types. It would also mean that replication of those types is being hampered somehow, and in fact, the KAD layer through the replication quorum may be trying to replicate older data and not the newer data because there's a quorum number of older data. Even though our nodes internally, in node internal logic, should be preferring the newer data. This quorum vs CRDT is likely an issue that we have to resolve.

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `22:16:42` **dirvine.** said:

Hey @Traktion If you were using non API calls previously by making private stuff public, then it's a tough call as the innards have indeed changed a lot to make streaming possible. There was old code in self encryption that was not good and using an incorrect cypher that meant there were differnet chunks created. It was not an issue as we had not made them public. 

I would really advise not using private calls in any crate like that as these have no guarantees in semantic versioning and will almost certainly be removed without notice. 

I am not sure of the way you are using the code, but can you please take a look at self encryption public API and if you see changes there that have broken your code please let us know as that would be a contractual break on our side and not good at all. I hoep we have not done that, but I doubt it would have slipped through so many of us. 

If you can have a look again I would appreciate it. 

There was a part of self encryption we did not use in autonomi on purpose, it should nto have bene in the API and I think it is now removed, but if you got caught there then it's on us for sure.  We would need to try and do something, but that old code woudl have produced differnt chunks from the autonomi API for sure. It was wrong they were left in self encryption. In any case lets see what we can do here, but I fear you were using those and did expose some private parts of them to make them public, which will maybe be hard to resolve. We can try what we can though, but we woudl have an issue, fix that old stuff to use the correct cypher and break your old data or fix it to keep the wrong cypher to make your old data OK but maintain the fact self encryption will produce different data from different calls? 

A bit deep, but lets work on it

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `22:21:40` **dirvine.** said:

In terms of data_map changes @Traktion there are 2 API Calls to shrink a data map (make it from ol to new type) and also get root data_map (take a new type and get the old type from it).  These use functors to define the chunk store. 
In the API for autonomi these are not needed and we tested the autonmi API for old and new data to ensure we don't need them, but for your case if you went direct to self_encryption then you may need to use them to get and old format data map if you wanted to use those older streaming methods (which are really random access as opposed to streaming). Anyway names aside, perhps this will help

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `22:48:42` **dirvine.** said:

There are two functions, like I was saying @Traktion These allow you to go from the shrunk data maps and to the shrunk data maps. They should be available in self-encryption. Let me check. Yes it's https://docs.rs/self_encryption/latest/self_encryption/fn.get_root_data_map.html
However that assumes you have access to teh chunk store. So this is a bit tricky but you can give it a functor that uses the network as the chunk_store. So a functor that downloads chunks will do that for you. 

There is another API call https://docs.rs/self_encryption/latest/self_encryption/fn.shrink_data_map.html to let you go the opposite way. 

There is also a parallel get root data map as well. 

However https://docs.rs/self_encryption/latest/self_encryption/fn.streaming_decrypt_from_storage.html will download a file of any size, but it does it in one go and write to a file, you could stream direct form the file, which may be simpler. I know Qi tested with this by downloading large movies and while downloading he was able to watch the movie. 

SO I thik we cna get there, albeit a bit of work. 

I am not saying this is the ultimate, but just to get you back up and running it would work. 

But the random access stuff you were using will likely still work if you get the root data map or indeed grab your old data_maps (which are already root data maps) 

It seems we do though  need to get an issue to check the random access self encryption parts and ensure 
- They also use new data_map formats 
- Do use the correct cyphers 

Which would appear to be th eultimate resolution so you can have that random access with new data as well and do so without haing to get_root_data_map() and so on

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `22:58:04` **traktion0_20257** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> There are two functions, like I was saying @Traktion These allow you to go from the shrunk data maps... [truncated]

Thanks @dirvine! I'll take a look at the links tomorrow, but it sounds promising. 

You're right about random access too, or at least reading from an offset to a limit. From a  HTTP perspective, the range headers are basically asking for this. The browser may ask for a specific byte range, etc.

The main thing is that the data is streamed at the HTTP end. Chunk-streamer reads a bunch of chunks and then outputs them as a stream of data to the HTTP client. AntTP essentially buffers the data chunk by chunk between self_encryption and the HTTP client.

So, maybe the naming semantics depend on perspective. Ultimately, the browser can stream 4k videos, without the full file being downloaded anywhere first, which is pretty cool! 😅
