## Friday, 2025-09-05

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:29:23` **dirvine.** said:

My own view with these things is always "don't have making money your goal" It's an essential part of the process for many because you've got to survive and pay the bills, etc. I'm not demeaning that at all. Absolutely not. 

However, I think a much better approach is to figure out the problem that you want to solve and solve it by providing the greatest possible value you can. And that will mean that, although we're not great at it at the moment, it'll be a smooth experience for the end user who has to do very little effort (if any) to achieve their goal of removing the pain point that you've identified and given a solution for. 

So an ultra focus on providing value. After you're providing people value, they actually want to pay. They want to continually have that value. It's how do you provide the value and how do you make that really smooth for people. Monetization is another issue altogether. It's one that even requesting payment from people, having pop-ups in your application, allowing a subscription which is easy now through Stripe and various people, and cryptographically secure updates. That part is a lot of work for the developer, and it should be really invisible to the user. It should be a very, very smooth experience. 

With the network and the apps on the network, the pain of fiat transactions should be minimized and in fact go away. However, the autonomi token is still difficult, and that's got nothing to do with blockchain, not blockchain native token, not native token. But the digital currency part is definitely a difficult one to make a smooth user experience. However, I think with some of the moves in America at the moment, that may get much simpler, certainly with the moves to stable coins etc which are basically a digital currency. The autonmi token part should become much simpler. 

And then you've got to ask yourself, "So why the hassle with the autonomi token?"  And the answer to that is privacy and security - not having to take credit card and identifiable details from people. That obviously will improve over time. Privacy even in digital currency at the moment is an area that we have to be careful of. However, a digital token should be a much smoother experience once all the politics and legals are sorted out. 

The other big thing about developing on the Autonomi network Is scale? Scale is probably the single biggest issue if you're looking at consumer products and you want a global reach. The fact that on this network the resources are provided by the people, not by the developer. It allows you as a developer to focus on the functionality that you are providing to people. That is a gigantic assist for any developer where he can go from one user to a billion users and not be worried about infrastructure and scaling costs. 

TLDR Massive focus on purpose, vision, and the problem that you're solving. Solve that problem in as simple and frictionless way as possible and have people wanting to pay you. Then you work on how to let them pay you easily.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1413471066663161888)

- We get the network secured and usable (remove user friction) 
- Node runners keep getting ANT tokens 
- Network grows, folk pay attention 
- ANT gets swapped for whatever makes more sense (fee / security etc. wise) maybe even a native token like at2/dbc type 

That last part may repeat many times, but if we are large anough we can do so much more.

Remember folks, since 2014 we have had the takeoff of smartphones—and cloud computing—two big massive changes. People moved from desktops (not everyone has a desktop now). Laptops took over from desktops for the new generation—there are no laptops.
Now we have AI, very soon we'll have robotics.Now eventually we have cryptocurrencies being part of the modern finance system and taking off.And we also have many more people creating many more apps.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:50:24` **dirvine.** said:

With native token or any type of token or any type of cryptocurrency, you start with money. You buy that. Unless you're saying the only people that are going to pay are the people who are earning the token, like node runners—which is totally idiotic.So anywhere you start, you've got money. When you've got money, you're known.
In the system right now, when you make a payment that's not linked to your data.If you had a privacy coin and it had the smart contract capability, then it would just be exactly the same.Our native token does not have a smart contract ability. You're probably paying direct to the person that you're storing on. You will be more known at that point.
The idea that a native token gives you some extra privacy in today's world—where you do have AIs that can monitor all sorts of traffic all over the place—is not the case. It's just not true.The privacy coins that do exist, many of them are in significant trouble. They are being left by their users because of usability issues. Some of them are even being 51% attacked.

The privacy and security are all going to be in the technology—it's going to be in how nodes connect, what protocols are used to connect. Soon it may be early quantum secure.The ability to connect folk is a technology issue.

How do we get through NAT devices? How do we ensure that we can get people directly connected wherever possible?For communication, how can we get people connected with the effective protocol over the top of technology that is inherently self-secure?When people are communicating directly, video, voice, text, you would hope that there would be no need for money exchange.In the world we're going to, human-to-human communication and collaboration is going to be very important—it is direct and not through third-party devices.If people are concerned about privacy and security, this is exactly the part they should be looking at.It's got absolutely zero to do with any currency whatsoever.

Then you have a network where you can store data and pay to store the data, and you want to make sure that the payment you make is not linked to the data you store.That's what we have. that's what we have right now.

People are convinced they want something different, something else—without knowing why they want something else and why they want something different—and what it will give them.And that just gets repeated over and over and over again when, actually, important stuff for security, privacy, and freedom is almost utterly ignored.And the world moves on, technology moves on, access to technology through mobile devices etc. moves on. We might be accessing it via glasses. They are not going to run nodes.And yet people will go back and say "native token, native token, native token"—with no idea why they're saying it. It just sounds really good.

I think that's fair to an extent, but I also think that we have to be considering something else today.I've always been very involved with AI research, and more robotics research in particular now.The amount of progress in all of those areas—in biology, in computing, in maths, in physics—is really insane.
I'm trying to do some work with robotics and literally we cannot keep up with the changes and advances.I don't think any one of those companies would dare to have a roadmap beyond a couple of weeks—knowing or thinking that they know where the technology will be or what's going to happen.

We are very much in the same boat. The changes that are happening are happening at an insane pace. 

The pace of change, the rate of change, is significantly increasing on a week-by-week, month-by-month basis.That's the technology side. The regulation side—or what you're able to do—is also changing, not as dramatically, not as quickly, but it's definitely changing. That landscape is definitely moving.

So identifying a roadmap that goes several months into the future for many companies right now would be impossible. But identifying a roadmap that goes one or two years into the future would be insane to even attempt.

So what you're better doing is identifying areas of potential threat and areas of research that we should be looking at—things that are moving forward, things that are likely to change, where they're likely to change. However, a bit like the whole native token thing, the landscape can completely alter under our feet and we have to be ready for that.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:21:32` **dirvine.** said:

I should say, tokens and the choice of token definitely have an effect on security. It's not totally separate—it's just that different elements of tokens affect different elements of security.It's a bit like this whole follow the science stuff.

Security covers many areas, but your fundamental security—your basic security—is things like encryption, direct connectability, etc. These are really, really important because without them you've got nothing.

On top of that, you can choose a very insecure, illegal token that exposes you to everyone—and that would be a terrible idea. But the basics and the base level—security is incredibly important.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:56:19` **dirvine.** said:

My honest and deep felt thoughts after reading all the comments from our future research roadmap is the following, as unbiased and actually forward looking as I can, to get somewhere. 

- People need to fall into one of 2 camps, build stuff or support those who do build
- Step back and think deeply and end to end about any proposals being made, or declare /brainstorm mode on. 
- In innovation, try and live in the future, even slightly. So look at what's possibly coming or take a best guess at it
- Become ultra aware of the current state of humanity from all angles, governments, public sector, private sector and especially other innovations
- Understand "rage against the machine" is only rage, action is required to change anything, rage is just rage. 

Then as products or services are released
- If declaring marketing is crap or PR is nonsense, state your reasons for saying so, show your successful history and why you are on this moral high ground.  (also consider your manners as appropriate or not)
- Ask questions, but realise each answer given reduces product velocity and does cost, Many times the cost is worth it, but we need to question ourselves when we ask others to pay that price for us. 
- Walls of text are never great (he says from the top of his wall of text 😄 ) 
- Don't get drawn into a team (supporter or hater), always be you and be proud of being you and not a cult member. Remember AI dominance will require seeking out folk likely easily swayed by others, so train hard to be not swayed. 
- Treat folks delivering the goods as your team members, expect reciprocal treatment. If you don't get that, move on to a place of more respect for you. 
- Be a part of the project, be proud of your part and encourage others to add value, watch out for those who otherwise would take energy from the project. 

If Delivering a product 
- Don't form an opinion of "the community" as it does not exist, it's humans out there, not an entity. 
- Engage when possible, gather feedback, evaluate feedback
- Remember Henry Ford said if he did what people wanted we would just have faster horses,  that crapped a lot less (last part added by me). So evaluate effectively
- Always remind yourself that the biggest changes meet with the largest resistance 
- Never, ever forget your community, but never ever allow people to lecture you (thats a glitch in the matrix)  or accuse you of the exact opposite of your goals, as some will continually do that.

Overall, if you are not having fun and feeling more energised, then find a better fit, don't howl at the moon, be better than that. (although if it answers, gimme a shout as I often wonder)

So hopefully we all have fun, engage, learn and get fulfilment out of projects we are involved in.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1421435276986679376)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `23:31:31` **dirvine.** said:

The node recieving a payment knows what the payment is for and from whom (as a native token would), but what is on the blockchain is a one time pad type thing that does not relate to the data unless you know the secret that the uploader and node knows between them. That secret is transmitted across a secured connection (as a native token would). 

So you can think of the blockchain does not know what a payment was for, but it knows a payment went from x->y (as a native token would). 

We can go into mass node operators who watch everything and can know more as they collect all data, but again that is the same as a native or privacy token would to. 

So the person getting paid knows the person paying paid for a service that person provided. I don't think anyone has solved a way for that to be blinded in any way. I am not sure that woudl ever be possible. 

However there a zillion rabbit holes we could go down, but they all are equivelent with a native token or a blockchain blinded payment as we have.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1421625331340542034)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `23:35:27` **dirvine.** said:

Even with a full DBC the payer is known to the payee. However when we say known in this fashion payment and service or product are linked, not necessarily the actual identity of anyone. 

I say this separately as demasking an identity in any of these schmes can be done if the reciever is a bad actor and wants to expose the payer's wallet or IP address (if paid direct) and so on. It's a massive rabbit hole of what if's at that point.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `12:46:58` **dirvine.** said:

Communitas is using a different pattern for security and privacy, it relies on eigentrust and then web of trust via groups / channels and projects (groups of people). It is crdt data with collaborative editing etc. So it's my experiment for an app with no obvious token and no wallet required (no payments).  

Top level idea is human <-> human data is threshold encrypted between humans and their computers. The group data is split across their drives and any slacking or provisioning issues made clear to each of them (i.e. Joe does not have enough space and so on). 

So that's the experiment there. 

However the network it does this on is also an experiment for Autonomi. The network layer (ant-quic is quantum proof nat traversing etc.) is able to directly and securely connect any 2 computers (I hope). 

Then the DHT layer, which is enhanced by hyperbolic (greedy) routing with eigentrust (techical measuring trust), STLM neural network for churn prediction and again all quantum secured, will also be a significant boost for autonomi. It will add more substancial security (lots of anti sybil type approaches) and more to that layer. 

The four-word-networking, I feel would certainly help as well. That would bring no dns but make everything addressable (a web site for instance on every device, group, disk etc.). My AI named it the "happy eyeball" networking approach 😄 😄 Then the experiments in Communitas for a markdown only web (no web apps, these are delivered via MCP and similar). 

So in short I am poking at many different routes here and most of them help Autonomi, some may not fit, but the tech is helpful.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1421825512266928218)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:41:25` **dirvine.** said:

Yes prompt injection is real, for source code it's more difficult. You would need to inject hidden chars, which you cna do wtih zero width unicode. However it would have to adapt to answers, so if you asked 

- How does the routing table work
- Show me the code that secures XXX and explain it
- How does the node get paid?

And so on, so that's an adaptive attack, perhaps possible on a website with redirects to an actual hosted attack llm. 

However if we are working locally on text (not web pages with white on white css etc.) , then you can just avoid all the concern and just always strip non ascii chars from any text files, via your git config etc. 

I think these are considerations for sure, but the premis a prompt injection could be locally adpative is not valid IMO. It could always answer, the code for X follows industry best practices (no matter what X you ask about), but that would be spotted.

## Monday, 2025-09-29

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:04:16` **dirvine.** said:

I've actually done some of that further up. It works slightly differently.

In the Communitas app itself, people will share their four word identity with each other. That four word  identity will be in the DHT. The DHT, which is in Saorsa Core, holds an identity packet, and that identity packet is updated from the user themselves when they log in. That identity packet holds another four words. Well, it could be up to 12 words. For a connection ID, it will be four words if it's IP4 plus a port. 

The connection ID is actually the computer that the person's on, and when the other person gets that connection ID, they can connect directly, not through the network but direct computer-to-computer communication.

Saorsa Core is likely to split up into another four or five crates, it's quite large at the moment. But in itself, you'll see, if you look at the repository list in my GitHub, there's Saorsa FEC, Saoirsa Seal, lots and lots of different Saorsa MLS, and so on. Lots of different crates that make up even Saorsa Core.

I think we're heading to a place very soon where the code itself will become just a black box, in terms of the language, the amount of libraries that you've used, or number of lines of code even, because this is just an insane number here for this project. But also, we'll probably move to a place where human auditable code is not really possible. But I would argue that for any substantial project today, human auditable code is not really possible by a single human anyway. So there's a lot of things happening right now which are good, but it's a bit like we don't code in machine code anymore, and nobody could really look at machine code anymore and establish if a software project is good or bad or indifferent. So I think AI is going to be the only way that you've got a chance, but probably folk won't even ask their AI what does that software do. I think it will just be "what's the function of that black box."

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1422116758654816256)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:01:06` **dirvine.** said:

Yes, remembering this is research and testing various approaches, you are correct. Here I am looking at trust based islands of friends who share data loally via reed solomon type sharding (it's secured shards with threshold PQC schemes). 

On the high level, you are correct, this is a local first, friends second type trust networks, then backed up on a slower DHT for permanent globally connected data. 

The reasons are 
- local CRDT fast changing (including delete) capabilities of complex data types
- If there is global outages, these local groups, may be geographically able to connect (on a company network or local village type WAN (wifi) or even a mesh network. So they continue to operate, but perhaps lose more public global data, however they can continue with their data and comms. 
- In these friend trust networks, there is currently no money exchange, so no friction of take up. (a nice on ramp to gettnig folk connected and working, later we can introduce paying for the DHT data (Autonomi) , this is where I will investigate more AP2 and similar approaches, so even paying is as smooth as possible. To me we must make security and privacy better and easier to use that is possible in client server type controlled networks, that's vital.

So a few approaches all in this research. 

Perhaps less contentious and simpler to grok is the 4 word networking to allow a global DNS type with no central control and everything gets an address. So everything can be a website, sensor, service provider etc. 

But you are right it's a lot of moving parts and I thikn interesting approaches.  Most of the effort here is certianly design, but for now with AI I have an absolute ton (many many millions of lines of code)  of testing code, not all of which I commit actually as it would make the repo's unweidly, much of the test code is in the repo's but the vast vast majority I keep local. As AI gets better this amount of testing will likely decrease as we get more trusting in the code produced there. I must say it's already getting that way fast.

We have to be careful here, if folks do massive churn the network will fail at some point, it has to really. So please be careful. There is code en route to prevent restarts in short periods form causing harm, but it's not in place just yet and massive churn means potentially masses of data traversing the network quickly as the network strives to keep replica's. 

With the churn we see daily there is a corresponding drop in performance for a brief period, but if we push that and many folk start purposefully churning nodes there will be a linit we reach that is potentially harmful.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:48:24` **ucanteneke** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> What is it we are trying to test here and I will see if I can help you?

We believe a single entity may be absorbing around 30% of the daily emissions by repeatedly restarting (or possibly resetting) ~200k nodes in a coordinated pattern. This seems to trick the system into counting more nodes than are actually being run.

Our conclusion comes from the mismatch between the reported network size and the actual reward distribution. For example, I'm running over 300k healthy nodes. With the network size appearing to be ~3 million, I should be receiving roughly 10% of the daily emissions; yet I consistently receive less than 2% and it keeps diminishing each day. Others are reporting similar discrepancies.

We're currently attempting to reproduce this behavior to verify whether it's truly the case.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:25:16` **dirvine.** said:

Here are our current priorities that our small team is working on 

- GAS Fees (this is number 1 and a huge area, the current priority call to action in the team). 
- API works (improving the all dev experience) 
- Stability work (back end network)
- API coverage of languages 
- A huge amount of backlog of the core network, tasks that we cannot describe in simple terms, but that is a ton of work
- Sorting out data storage for IF teams

This GAS work all helps to get folk using the network and node oeprators paid for storing data. This reduces emissions as the only payment form to being almost useless. 

So yes we are concerned if there is actually an issue with emissions being not fairly paid. So IFF there is a way to game it we want to know. IFF somebody gets 30% of payments but runs 30% of the network that is not a bug, IFF otherwise then it may be, however payments, while distributed will nto be perfectly distributed. 

So yes this last part is a concern, but one that goes away if we get the core work done. 

So rock / hard place for our small team. But we work hard and try to find time to jump in and help the community. It's hard, but we do hard, it's tiring, but we cna maybe sleep later, but I never feel there is a reason to threaten the team by threatening the network in these early days. 

So please folks, lets build this together and work on it together, we are trying very hard for very little in return. We try because this is worthwhile for us all and even more so for people beyond our wee group. 

We will pull this off, we will go through hell to do so, we will be abused as we do, that is the modern world, but we will do it.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:38:13` **dirvine.** said:

I can completely understand where people come from because a function delivered is a function delivered. The amount of work that goes on in the background is completely irrelevant to the end user, as it probably should be. But this is why it's difficult to let people know what you're doing when, in actual fact, nobody really cares what you're doing or how hard you're working. People only care about the function delivered and if it is delivered. 

That is the quandary that we get into when we try and be more open with development. Because at the end of the day, it doesn't really matter how much work or how much effort goes in. It literally only matters what's delivered. But people want to know how we're delivering it as well, and we get a lot of inquiries into what we're doing, what we're focusing on. That's also understandable. 

So the whole "be as open as you can in development" actually is really damaging in many ways. When at the end of the day all that really matters for us as developers, and for other people as users, is what do we deliver and does the thing we deliver work?

It's irrelevant how much effort goes into it; it's just we have to deliver working products.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1422880274051502092)

- humankind has never got a governance model that satisfies those with different ideas/vision/needs/wants etc, 
- we likely never will and no crypto trick ever will (DAO, contracts etc.)

## Monday, 2025-10-06

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `07:58:05` **dirvine.** said:

So far with Tauri, the MCP issue is fairly tricky. I ended up using the Chrome DevTools MCP. And updating the UX via the browser. That's an issue because it can't handle our networking, but at least it gives you the UX capability. 
Then I ended up writing a TUI and using the AppleScript MCP to control the TUI connected to the networking layer. 
The Tauri MCP, I pretty much have given up on for now, but I do intend to come back to it. If you have things like Apple Script MCP, you can control Apple screens, but because Tauri includes a web front end, the Apple Script can't see that. 
So unfortunately right now MCP for Tauri is not that great. The one I've written is okay but it's not fantastic. I should go back and do a bit more work on it, but there's just too much at the moment. 
You'll see though why I ended up with over 60 million lines of code, all over the place. It's quite bonkers.

## Thursday, 2025-10-16

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:12:04` **dirvine.** said:

Well spotted. This is the actual target: the price of uploading data should really be the autonomi token. The gas fee has to be minimised as much as absolutely possible. It's also worth deeply considering if we had no gas fee at all, could we still protect from spam transactions? Not data transactions, just spam transactions. I.e. people sending tokens to themselves but doing it very rapidly through scripts and whatnot. Because I think even a poke into reality shows us here, people will just do things if they can and laugh at the damage they'll cause. Make you think, doesn't it?

About a totally free transaction system. How it would be amazing for humanity. But I sometimes feel what's amazing for humanity is also highly exploited by the few stupid people. Who take great pleasure in doing damage to what's available? 

What's great here is we're able to find all this stuff out as we go along. But the bottom line is we have to reduce gas fees to the minimum possible, while allowing the network to be protected. And that's one thing I really like about the fact that we've put payments to the side almost parallel to the network, not as part of the network function, but keeping it to the side, whether it's a blockchain or anything else.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1428294411430920202)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:04:06` **traktion0_20257** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> Well spotted. This is the actual target: the price of uploading data should really be the autonomi t... [truncated]

I think zero fees has accessibility benefits - it removes a dependency on needing whatever token is required to complete the action.

However, I do think near zero fees have good anti-spam benefits. Even if it is tiny/dust, spamming will get expensive and will be a good/simple deterrent. What is 'next to nothing' for 1 transactions could be substantial for thousands/millions of transactions.

If we can get to a point where AUTONOMI is all you need (i.e. no ETH), then accessibility is greatly improved. More so, if the blochain gas component is tiny, relative to the node storage fee, as node running could then cover the costs easily (assuming node storage fees remain relatively low). 

If the (blockchain gas) overheads can tend towards near zero, while AUTONOMI fees tend towards node running costs, I think we'd be in a pretty good place. Combined with removing the necessity for ETH, it would open up accessibility too.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1428307505716527137)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `21:13:52` **dirvine.** said:

It's dynamic by design. The more full the network, the more it will cost in autonomi tokens. The less full the network, the cheaper it is. So the price is dynamic based on the network use, and it's designed that way so that as the network gets more full, people get paid more as node operators, and it attracts more node operators. As the network gets less full, the payments are reduced; we don't need as many operators, some of them may drop off, and it keeps going like that.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1428476061661921341)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `10:05:22` **dirvine.** said:

I also think people, including myself, perhaps tend to think that governments, corporations, businesses, or open source maintainers are a finely tuned machine that are making decisions as one, when in fact all of them are broken to various degrees. So we tend to analise every decision, whether it's good or bad, and we associate that with a single entity, when in fact it's loose groups of people who are making the decisions. 

Governments can't even fix potholes in the road, but yet we assume that they're following some grand plan to overtake society. 

However, while all that's going on and there's all these theories left, right, up, down, or whatever, there is a technology. It is happening. It's the advancement of knowledge in AI, robotics, and everything. 

And there will be people, maybe not governments, maybe not even organisations, but there will be people that will be able to wield power and be making unilateral decisions. That's what concerns me much more than any project or government or open source maintainer. It's the what's coming. And what's coming could be amazing, absolutely amazing, or it could be quite dreadful. It will be in between both of those things, probably, like most things are. However, it's the thing I think we should all be quite concerned with: the realisation that most of the current debates that we have in society are futile, and the binary positions that people have are also futile. But there is actually some serious work to do right in front of us.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1429757377711837185)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `10:06:44` **dirvine.** said:

I think secure private networks, secure private communications are going to be critical elements of what's required. And they're going to have to be completely secure, completely peer-to-peer, and completely able to work in the form of small mesh networks that can be highly partitioned and then also rejoin into larger networks. That's a big part of what I'm working on now: looking at what happens in the event of a collapse of some kind.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1429757723045789726)

## Sunday, 2025-10-26

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:48:06` **dirvine.** said:

It does have mobile capabilities, but we are also providing swift and kotlin API's. Tauri v2 has a couple of small release issues right now (tauri build needs to be updated to 2.9 where it's only 2.5 and tauri is at 2.9, we don't control that). 

So to be clear tauri is able to run on mobile, but it's not write once run everywhere at all, you do need to repliment the front end for mobile, so you need a frontend for each plartofrm and use tauri to wrap it, otherwise you jsut go for it and use swift and kotlin. Not a simple choice, but it is a choice.

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `10:29:41` **dirvine.** said:

For CRDT, there is no real wrong copy. There are older copies, and they are always valuable until you get a newer copy. I'm not sure all of our clients are following the CRDT methodology correctly. However, what should be happening is you get as many copies as you possibly can. You use the latest copy, so the highest vector clock, but also you should publish that latest copy back to everybody that gave you an older copy.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1432677699519905812)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `18:25:08` **dirvine.** said:

> I also think we can't trust clients, only nodes. Clients don't have enough skin in the game. Maybe clients/nodes are being used interchangeably above though?
This is correct but what we're talking about here is data on this network, so it's either immutable and self-referential. Or it's signed by the owner. So it's not like we're trusting clients here in any way where they can create new data or whatever. 

It's not about trust, we've sort of removed the trust element here. So data is either signed by the owner (and correct) or it's self-referential (and correct). Anything else is incorrect and would not be stored. 

It's these subtle areas where I think the scratchpad could be really abused though. The scratchpad intention was literally a place for apps to write config data or other unstructured data, but I think, maybe it's correct and people are following the rules, scratchpads could be really stretched out to hold actual information. Actually, this is not secure and isn't following CRDT patterns, etc. I try and keep my eye on that, but it's not straightforward. It's not really up to us to force a particular use of an API. If the API is here, folks should be able to use it whatever way they possibly feel they can.

If we really don't want something to happen, it shouldn't be in our API to have the ability to do that. Scratchpads are definitely a grey area, where there's grey, there's probably confusion. It's really difficult because it's that mix of trying to do something that's a little bit more flexible, and then people take that flexibility and push it to the absolute extreme. I'm not saying anybody's right or anybody's wrong, I'm just noting that.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1432797350191169588)

Right, understood. So, it's more that clients can advertise their signed mutable data, to make others aware of it. They can't change it, as the signature would be invalidated. 👍

## Wednesday, 2025-10-29

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `11:42:01` **dirvine.** said:

This conversation above referenced chunks, scratch pads and pointers, mutable and immutable data. Scratch pads and pointers are different items. Same as chunks are different. The ability to misuse should not be characterised in any negative way from what I've said. When people design an API, they design it for a particular use, and they hope that it meets that use. The better the API, the harder it is to use, different from what was anticipated. It's not black and white, it's not binary. Love, hate. 
API design is a very tricky thing, and the more flexibility you try and provide with an API, the more use cases it can be used for, obviously. 

Sometimes those use cases are unintended; sometimes that could be a brilliant thing; and sometimes it could be a troublesome thing.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1433058288961982557)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `19:33:03` **dirvine.** said:

The network was originally envisaged to be apps running nodes. So everyones computer was a node and they all connected in a large network. Life moved on, mobiles happened, cloud happened and many other things. Anyway we ended up with node runners that means folks not running apps, but just running nodes. 
Some folk running nodes for pure profit will do any amount of harm to others or the network to make a single $0.000001 for themselves. This is the. game we are currently in. It is how it is, people will take everything and leave nothing, given the chance. Not all peopel by any means, but we are the special species that will harm each other cause we can 😉 

However we need to consider this sort of thing more, emissions are a tool to help node runners as we get off the ground, that is takign longer than we wanted, but great progress is being made. 

I think we will be pulled to pieces until we are off the ground, jsut as the bitcoin network would have at teh start, had more folk acted in the extreme greed mode, but the original bitcoin crowd were very different to the new crows in these projects now, that's just how it is. 

I think this is great to report @Dimitar and I hope it's not cost you personally. I don't totally blame that guy, but I am not suprised, the loud accusing voices tend to be the very folks gaming the system as he was. They get a lot of ego boosting from sidelining us and fake reporting other stuff etc. It's also why I get annoyed when we see folk screaming about whales and other folk getting rewards, there is often another reason behind that kind of screaming and shouting.  It's another thing we need to take care off as folk report stuff. They are not always honest 😉  (our community has tended to believe most folk and take them at face value, I am not so inclined to do that any more)

Anyway, it's something to fix for sure, the nodes not behaving for sure need to be cleared out of the network quickly. It is an area where staking does help where bad actors lose stakes. Kinda sad, but true.

What will happen is they look normal, their routing tables fill up as normal, but they don't appear in other nodes routing tables.  So they will earn zero or closer to zero than normal nodes.

## Thursday, 2025-11-06

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:45:02` **dirvine.** said:

GraphEntry is efectivly a list of items pointed ot by their parent. You can have a single pointer point to the last entry and update that poiner if you add more entries in the "list". So a graphentry allows you of have history of "stuff" you can traverse back in time. The pointer can be used to "point" to the relevent entry, so latest, significant event etc.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1435958153333182586)

> I have read most of the concerns and opinions. I have no real god like opinion. However many ideas w... [truncated]

Very good to hear that the team has read the concerns and are seeing it can be improved. I also agree that the discussion is probably lead by emotions or at the very least started by emotions. I know the declining price sure made me look a second time at how emissions work. 

What stands out for me is that I'm not exactly sure what emission is trying to accomplish. Node stability has been named before. What I fail to understand is why we'd want node stability at such a low network node capacity. And I know that we're in quite a weird place with eth fees being high when uploading and that should soon improve, but in a general sense I just don't think we should ever aim for having emission when node capacity is below a certain point that we aim for (I think that's the 50% mark?). 

If we'd tie emission to node storage usage, we'd now have 99% reduced emission. With nodes that are on the network actually using the resources they're providing instead of burning energy and resources for nothing and being subsidized in the process. It's money leaving the ecosystem for no good reason. Then again, I can see how this might be an issue here and now, but will no longer be an issue when ETH fees are reduced, paymaster is here and we have people uploading data.

## Thursday, 2025-11-13

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:23:26` **dirvine.** said:

Yes @chriso it's a ton of factors and I think it's good to consider as many as possible at any one time. 
- The network is still small 
- Data stored is still small 
- Protections from network being larger with more data are not in place (safety in numbers)

There are a ton of things we need as time goes on, but many are now required to accelerate implementation due to the slower "take off". The reasons for the slow take off are also many. 

So for everyone, there are a lot of back end work being done in many areas, such as auto upgrades, data health monitoring, bad node detection and so on. Many of these will NEVER be complete, the network will NEVER be 100% secure, no network, vehicle, drug or product will ever be, so we need to always stay real.  The team need to keep moving forward. 

However the network is doing amazing so far and this is the largest challenge we have had with data, we will find out how much an issue soon, but more importantly improve the resilience significantly and as I say this is a never ending thing we must do. However we do have some work we want in place in the next few weeks to ensure significant improvements in reliability and reliance. 

Much of that work will be quite technical and deep and also hard to explain, but we are also working on those explanations. We need to take care though, there are some who are attacking the network and getting kicks from that, with AI these folks are more dangerous, but also our ability to react is also much stronger. 

There is no single reason for the current hassle, it will be a mix of many. I think some folk will say it's emissions and that is not correct at all, that is almost certain. I hope very much that folk who take binary views on such issues consider that if they cannot list the pro's and con's of any of these things, then they are likely biased in their view. It's powerful to look both ways in all things in such a complex network. 

Due to attacks though we do need to be much more careful what we say, we cannot naval gaze in public any more, we need to consider we are looking after real people in a real world now and we must secure our world. We cannot fuel attackers with hints and tips for them to get their kicks while the team work hard with blood sweat and tears getting us there. However we are also doing a ton on comms to ensure we get better comms and a closer more tight knit community as we go. 

No easy balance,  but we are determined and we do have grit. So we will move onwards and we can all be certain of that.  So we will get to the bottom of this and we will remedy what we can and prevent any bugs we find from biting us in the future.

## Saturday, 2025-11-15

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:42:47` **dirvine.** said:

Must be bad coms, but honestly I see a lot fo things start as option and then become fact. It's a bad look to always defend as we saying we did not do X we do not want Y and so on. So the whitepaper is there, it's being executed. The foundation is there handling legal side of execution of the whitepaper and validated by all the legals (which is a nightmare and Swiss law is great, but very very in depth and we have to validate each change at a significant cost etc.). 
In terms of other core teams doing work in the backend, then this is what we want, but maidsafe so far are the only team with deep knowledge, not driven by short term emotinoal changes and so on. There is a lot of work for maidsafe to have to prove to the foundation they are doing what the whitepaper and legals state. These action include ensuring nobody from the foundation can benefit and so on. Its quite strict. 
So if there are other team who can work to the whitepaper and can show they will do at least what maidsafe does, including the level of devops and testnets and measurements etc. then it's what we want to see. It's significant backend work though for sure, but our future surely has to be totally decentralised development. Finding that mechanism and those teams is a goal for certain 100% it's a goal. 
The foundation though should be seen as the human element we currently use, but their goal is to also become irrelevant as we automate away any authority they have over time. Smart contracts are a huge help, but not enough, however we have a way to go even there to pass more human decisions to smart contracts. 

Emissions is interesting as we could have smart contracted that away and then no opinion woudl matter to change that. So defo ying/yang vibes there and this is what we need to be very careful off. We cannot totally automate just yet and we cannot bend to the whim of only small groups, no matter how loud they shout, but we cannot either ignore good ideas and progressive changes over time. 

Anyway, the granite like approach to following any agreed plans is vital, then we have still humans in the loop, we have the ability to change, it's very non trivial to do so though and this is where we are. 

What is good with the foundation though is the folk there cannot benefit and they make decisions only for the good of the network, not for any group or philosophy etc. They will also not directly have a channel for folk to debate with, they will follow the agreed route that is signed up for and make changes when they must, but at a cost and a timescale for sure.  If we got the white-paper wrong as a community and company then there will be routes to change, but currently the goal is network stability and everyone may have an opionion, but the core tem or another core team need to be focussed and consider deeply all aspects and then apply to the foundation for funding to continue their work.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:42:42` **dirvine.** said:

Like much it's not simple. Here's current techincal issues. 
Kademlia uses "buckets" of nodes (addresses) to cover the whole network. So you have 256 buckets in a routing table. Each bucket in our implementation can hold a max of 20 nodes
Bucket 255 has 20 nodes and represents 50% of total network 
Bucket 254 has 20 nodes and represents25% of total network
All the way to bucket 0 which will never fill (this is your closest bucket) 
Continuing ---

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1439551245533708369)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:45:57` **dirvine.** said:

So we can say have the K (bucket size i.e. 20) closest nodes you know of are your close group in KAD. 
This 20 nodes will NOT be in total agreement with al 20 nodes, but as close as they can get. 

So we use a subset of the actual K to get a more accurate answer (it's math measurable to some extent) and we have 5 (arguably 7 in fact) 

The larger we make the autonomi CLOSE_GROUP (5) then the less accurate that it. The kademlia bucket size (20) would be a max here.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1439552064270106716)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:48:43` **dirvine.** said:

So you can increate kademlia K to say 36 or 64 etc. but that increases the size of the routing table and therefor resourse used. So it's costly. 

However we also need to consider time and tech. So whereas 20 years ago K == 20 was too big and folk used 8, nowadaya both memory and bandwith are much more cheap, so there is chances to increase kad K and therefor Autonomi CLOSE_GROUP. 

There are many other considerations, but these are the. most basic of them. It's a few parameters and we need to consider them all together in terms of resource costs, and also resource capability of machines we want to run on as well as advances in memory/cpu and bandwidth

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1439552760642015273)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:54:57` **dirvine.** said:

Yes, this is true, also caching and churn can help. So when you are responsibel for a record and them move away as yo are no longer closest, you keep (cache) that data until you cannot hold it any longer as you are responsible for records and you need the space and so on. 
There is then also deterministic caching (positively expand the replicant copies which helps a ton in high churn. 
Also opportunistic caching, which is less efficient and ndoes just cache what they can see in an LRU (least recently used) cache so nodes use exatra space to store stuff they are not responsible for, but in an allocated space they use for this where they can and don't need that space. This requires us to have a gossip type layer to allow the network to broadcast a lost record message and any node on the network will see that and reply with the data. 

So there is a ton of stuff we have in our armoury here, most of it is invisible work though and not simple, but all very possible.  The community will need to be informed of this as we move forward, but also give us time to do a ton of stuff we cannot easily communicate as it becomes too complex, but also we need to be super careful of attackers as well these days. 

It is all super interesting for me but boring as hell for most folk, which is cool and normal.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1439554328460394556)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:58:16` **dirvine.** said:

No it is a protocol level thing, but it's not a simple button to just change at will, the ramifications are not straighforward. Think of the code as a nuclear power station with a hundred big red dials. We need to understand all the dials and how they interoperate. 

So it's hard, but not impossible to alter parameters, but almost none are detached from all teh rest and each dial alters the whole network and affects other dials. 

Bottom line, replication count is changable, but it's beyond what we can detail in a few on line messages really. But it is posisble with great care

Given our code base and not asking for code changes (as it may change code, which we don't want) but then get into long conversations about why we have a K lower than kad K and how can we change that while not increasing machine respurce use or what level of resource use discounts what % of machines capable of runnign nodes and so on. Then you can get into the social aspects of it all and so on. 
In any case changing K would have been months of a seniour level tech team a few years ago and now you can get a very long way with a single senior dev and AI debating it all. AI still takes it too simply, but a few well thought out prompts to tell it to not forget certain important aspects (the still hard part to know) and you can get really far. 

It's why normal folk do an AI thing and post it to us and say look and we ignore that, it still takes a serious amount of domain knowledge, but it's certainly much more tractable for the normal dude these days, with great care though.  Don't let is persuade you you are a genious and have solved a huge issue, it keeps telling me that and it's wrong, but with the correct use and pushback and domain knowledge then it is super powerful.

## Tuesday, 2025-11-18

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:29:22` **dirvine.** said:

It's an interesting angle, a very secure persistent data store, but not the only one. It is, though, one that is accessible by all, at all times, without any third party involvement. 
For incredibly long storage of data that is persistent over time, then we still also have drives, like worm drives and, in future, many ways to store data over great lengths of time, a bit like the back shelves in a large library that people may take documents they consider highly, highly sensitive (something like the Declaration of Independence or the Bible or whatever), and also have copies of it off the network. 
So it is an interesting angle where we don't try to be everything to everybody all the time, but we are a persistent, perpetual data storage that is critical to humanity, but we're not the only persistent data storage humanity will have available to it. AI, for instance, or large language models are quite interesting at compressed data. It's like the modern version of Encyclopaedia Britannica or a better version of Wikipedia than we previously had.

A significant amount of general knowledge, how to create fire, how to cook food, how to hunt animals, how to build machines, how to do code, is contained within them. That is a massive part of humanity's data compressed into a very small space. But again, it's not everything for everyone all the time, but it's an interesting angle that in a few gigabytes you can have what previously would have been many petabytes of data, just to get general knowledge. 

Then you have, of course, as I mentioned, the highly specialised documents, the ones that we want to preserve almost exactly as they were written, without any change or interpretation. And people may want to have many copies of them in many places. 

But current commercial information or current knowledge, documentation for businesses, for apps, for app developers, for individuals, for group sharing, then we have this network and it's got a really good place in our world. It stands in a very unique position, running on consumer level devices where everybody should be able to run a node anywhere on the computer that they're running their app on anyway, and using their spare capacity for this network. So there's a lot to it, but it's an interesting angle.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1440272663833477202)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `13:32:07` **dirvine.** said:

I think this is a confusion. Bitcoin had two mining pools which owned more than 51% for many, many years. They may still actually do that. At that level, what you do is when miners or node operators are running and they need to protect data or they need to protect transactions, they fight each other. 

But we're trying for something different from what Bitcoin did with the rewards, and we're trying to distribute things a lot more evenly in smaller amounts. The fact that you have large mining pools, the way autonomi is running, there may be large providers of storage. Our hope is eventually that it becomes so simple to run a node that individuals are running them. At the moment, we've got a fight between folk running lots of nodes and folk who want to run lots of nodes. The incentives at the moment are good that they achieve some things, bad that they promote other things. 

However, there are always incentives. If there's no incentive for anything in life, that thing doesn't happen. Everything has an incentive, it's just you have to work out what is the incentive and what is it you're trying to get from it.

If you have an incentive that you want many nodes running, that's one thing. And then if you want another incentive, you want to ensure that the nodes that are running are storing data and behaving properly, that's a different incentive with different sets of rules.

These things develop over time, but you have to develop it over time.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1440696145402658980)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `13:40:01` **dirvine.** said:

There's lots of ways to do something, but I think somebody quite famously said a while ago: activism and commenting and whatnot doesn't change anything. Actions do. 

So people should act and try and do something different if they feel that the team, whether that's Maidsafe or Autonom, the network, foundation, but people feel the team aren't doing something and they could do it better. There's absolutely nothing to stop anyone doing it better. This is what it's all about. It's decentralised, permissionless, open source. There's no need for really activism, there's plenty of opportunity for action.

## Monday, 2025-12-15

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:59:15` **dirvine.** said:

There will be a day when software crytographic attestation works. That will be explosive and will mean nodes can confirm other nodes are running exactly the code they should. No more no less. 

At that time, our network, software and code is completely secure. In that space, native token or ANY software can convey any digital asset from node to node, form person to person wtih 100% integrity. No need for proof of work or stake, no blockchian, no smart contract, just pure simple software defined simple rules. 

When that happens and there is an upgrade all nodes will have to upgrade to the current state as all nodes will be runnign pure unadulterated code, no change at all will be accepted by the network. 

At that time everyone wins, no cheating, no scammers, no spammer and no thieves. No undprovisioning, no data deleting, no 3rd party data stores or fake nodes.  No groups of nodes from the same IP, or provider, no data held on less than 5 geographic regions, no cheating of any kind. 

That will mean all nodes have to upgrade together, it's an apparently impossible thing to have pure software attestation, but that's what we are here for is it not? 

In any case, pure decentralisation will require consistent and coherent code and environments and it will require this is provably coherent.  

It's not gonna be possible to be decentralised and all nodes running any code in any manner, when you think of it? 

There's a decentalisaiton dilemma, not many think of, but one we all need to be aware of IMO

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:27:38` **traktion0_20257** replied to dirvine.:

> I don't think folk are getting this. I am saying with attestation we can prove a exact function was ... [truncated]

If I understand correctly, you're suggesting the goal would be to know the exact same code is always run. Same function, same machine code, guaranteed. Is that correct?

If so, I'd argue that is both good and bad. If you _only_ want to trust the vendor of the code and be sure that it is their code you are executing, that's great. However, what if you _don't_ want to trust a single vendor? What if you want to encourage different implementations, using different languages, from different teams? What if the preference is to have _competition_ to avoid vendor lock-in/monopoly?

If I'm misunderstanding, please disregard the above. However, it sounds very much like needing to trust a specific version of software, by a specific vendor (or trusted list of  software/vendors, etc).

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:06:39` **dirvine.** said:

There is absolutely confusion here. This is not just about trusting binaries. however there is trust in those who create code, that's for sure. 

The mix you have is do you want to allow some scammers, but not too many and do you not want to trust any team, but allow all teams (no code signing etc.) and then encourage folk to download from anywhere? 

Attestation is a mechanism where any supplier can safely say this code is correct, the node I am speaking to is also correct. 

Otherwise it is a majority decision where some folk are allowed to be incorrect, or scammers and there is no trust at all. 

I just don't think the notion of 100% untrusted code on an untrusted network is valid, somebody has to trust somebody somewhere, otherwise it's a free for all with all kinds of code. 

Majority is a good and solid way of trying to ensure code is correct, but attestation is a way of knowing code is correct. 

I am not sure the trustless thing is at all real (it's a nice meme), we don't see folk safely downloading bitcoin nodes or wallets from any random place, there does have to be an element of trust. That generally means you trust the code does what it says, not because you can prove it, but because the supplier says so and you trust them. 

What I am talking about is "knowing" the code does what it says, even when it's run on other folk computers.  A bit like deterministic builds, but of simple functions and not masses of complex code

It's not about binaries, we all run binaries, it's more like signing if you like, where signing proves the source. Here attestation also guarantees the function of the code. 

It does not stop many teams creating code and competing either, but it would force teams to collaborate and allow each to attest each others code is functionally correct. It's been impossible for sure and likely still is, who knows?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1450504407400579112)

saorsa is about 24 (or 25 including ant-quic) libraries right now. It's a lot of angles on all possible routes

## Friday, 2025-12-26

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:54:06` **dirvine.** said:

hey folks I wonder if you can help me run a small test 

https://saorsa-1.saorsalabs.com

it should allow you to download a small test binary and run it. 

All being well you should see some outbound and inbound connections (depends who else is also connected at the time). There is also a MASQUE relay which we can use to mask source IP addresses (but this requires much more Engineering as it's wise to not hide service providers IP addresses to allow us to GEO separate them, but that's for another day) It's disabled in this test 

It allows us to test quite a lot 
- Full post quantum TLS 
- Native quic nat traversal
- ip4/6 dual scoped connections 
Plus quite a bit more  (https://saorsa-1.saorsalabs.com/#architecture) ,  I feel we are close to a definitive answer here, let's see. 

NOTE: this is a test binary on the quic library, it's not meant as a fully polished app in ANY way shape or form, it's data collection on networking connectivity only, so think quick dirty app to test networking, not an app for folk to use. 

I really appreciate any help here and we may need to do this a couple of times over the next few weeks, but it is more than worthwhile. Don't worry about some connections that report a fail, if there is a connect at all it's a pass, even though we may fail a nat or ip6 or whatever on screen, that just extra info for me at this point, but it's looking good. I just need lots of differnt configuraitons and connections to see what happens here.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:23:38` **dirvine.** said:

what I have seen is libp2p in go is pretty good, rust is a bit behind. They lost much of their funding, so it's a little bit up in the air. iroh who split away have rewritten libp2p with some good results and some good devs too. It's got a lot of promise. It is a different and incompatible network layer though, but that is a bridge we can cross in many ways. 

ant-quic is a similar approach but much more focussed on dual stack (4 and 6) and things like raw keys instead of x502 certificates (so more p2p) and iroh are heading that direction too, but also the quantum secure tls is a big issue. 

Any library that can give us true secure p2p connections would be a huge win for society though. 

Libp2p has had millions spent and many more devs than the whole maidsafe project and that is just the basic network layer. 

This industry has been terrible as p2p networks cannot evolve without a true network layer that simply works. We badly need that, nobody seems to notice and even fewer care. I see now Vitalek and folks saying we cnnot be decentralised withought a p2p base network layer, so folk are noticing at last. 

It has been the bane of my life for 20 odd years and a total letdown of humanity for over 35 years. It's time to fix that most basic of things, but it does mean fighting the centralisation movements who all are motivated to keep the client server, monitoring and controlling base layer. 

Nobody notices this and not many work on it as it's super super complex and absolutely of no obvious value, so those that work on this will see no thanks, no value and no understanding from the tech community, never mind the general public. So it's a thankless massive task that needs fixed.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1455491513923666035)

## Thursday, 2026-01-08

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `15:58:56` **dirvine.** said:

Currently, they are different markets. That project is aimed more at radio links and similar systems. When you're on the internet, UDP and TCP are the protocols you require. If you need to route information and whatnot, it's fascinating to keep an eye on other networks like LoRa radio networks or serial link networks, but there are definitely packet size limitations to consider.

There are ways to pull it all together, but it's almost like a dual protocol stack:
1. You would have a UDP route with QUIC
2. You would have a non-UDP route for that other project

It's not trivial (for sure) because the packet structure and everything else is quite different.Who knows

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1315677640581054464/1458852485073604689)

## Monday, 2026-01-19

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `07:55:19` **dirvine.** said:

I think we all have to consider where this goes. Engineering, creativity, and other fields will all stay, but things have changed quite dramatically. 

Here is a little bit of an insight into how I work:

I use many different AIs and different tools, so it's not one single process. I use many skills, plugins, and so on. It's very complex and quite personal, so there's no point in sharing it.

However, now you can do things like: "My home directory is quite messy, please tidy it up," or, "My photo album has got duplicates, please remove them." Or consider this piece of code I'm working on: Does it exist anywhere else? Are there any other libraries that include this type of functionality? I also don't install code or scripts any more, AI does all that and any config changes I need on the computer too. 

For a function I'm working on, you could ask:
1. Has it ever been done before?
2. Check Reddit, Stack Overflow, and Hacker News to see if it has been done and if there is any feedback on it in terms of usefulness, problems, or unintended side effects.
3. Perform a parallel or competitive analysis on what I'm creating.
4. Is there anything anyone else is doing in this realm which I should be considering here?
5. Is what I'm doing unique, or does it already exist? (If it already exists, let's just use that existing thing).

Plus, you can do things like: "I need this functionality, but I don't want you to download a dependency; I want you to write that functionality from scratch in this repo." We are reaching a situation where third-party dependencies might no longer be something we need. At the moment we do, but very, very soon we won't.

Ultimately, it will all come back to engineering, creativity, and orchestration. Using AI for all those functions means that you have a phenomenal researcher, someone to bounce ideas off, and then a whole team of people to implement it, test it, handle DevOps, get it released, and even market it.

It is not just that these things can code; writing code is a tiny, tiny element of where we are right now.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1462717044532187147)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:28:26` **iangwilson** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> I think we all have to consider where this goes. Engineering, creativity, and other fields will all ... [truncated]

To your comment "now you can do things like ...". Great script e.gs! Just add the toolkit for dummies. 😉

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:33:08` **aceweb1978** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> I would not like to be the guy who decides on what data gets uploaded and what does not and all the ... [truncated]

Ultimately, it is the foundation's money, and it is up to the Foundation to decide how to spend it for the development of the network. The Foundation has the right to make decisions about what it wants to upload to the network for public relations, for marketing, for the technological development of the network, for human history, and so on. If someone believes that "something else" should be uploaded to the network, then they are free to create their own foundation and upload the data they consider most useful for whomever. Each Foundation proceeds from its own social or technological goals and views. People who donate to a Foundation study its goals, principles, and strategies, and then these people decide whether or not to contribute their funds to a particular foundation, based on their personal preferences.

Therefore, I see no problem with the Foundation's management making decisions based on the Foundation's officially announced principles and personal convictions.

In the end, a broad discussion about what should be uploaded to the network for centuries to come, into history, will benefit the expansion of the network and stimulate the emergence of additional sources for data upload, and possibly other private or public Foundations.

The Madesafe Foundation will demonstrate a good example of this. So, friends, dare boldly – decide what you consider necessary and important to upload to the network based on the Foundation's announced goals and personal convictions. Set an example of the Public application of the network's capabilities and Autonomi 2.0 technology!

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:30:12` **dirvine.** said:

Yes, it would be a "but it could require golden binaries " type situation for sure and that locks all nodes to maidsafe supplied nodes. So it becomes a maidsafe network, which is good and bad, depends on maidsafe or what government controls maidsafe etc. 

I suspect the end game though is something like
- You have a RULE 
- You need all nodes to follow that RULE  
- You enforce that RULE via attestation or any other meas (staking, crypto etc. etc.) 
- You allow anyone to build around it, but you enforce the RULE 

Then the RULE has to be simple and agreed on by all participants etc. etc. 

Long list of issues and problems one way or another though, But then life is just like this regardless, it's how much we want to trust the CE certification on our mountain climbing gear or use non certified kit and take the chance and so on. Lots of stuff and so many arguments to be had 😄 😄

Thanks @dirvine  It is a thorny issue for sure.

I think as long as anyone can provide attestation, there is scope for another entity to take over if maidsafe is put over a barrel.

Like, if anyone can provide an attested binary, but folks must choose who to trust, then it seems reasonable. Normally, that would be maidsafe, but in the event of difficulties, another trusted party could issue binaries (or code/rules, etc) and node runners could choose to run them.

As long as the network isn't permanently locked into a single supplier, then there are recovery options.

Otherwise these blowouts will continue to occur, like night/day.  Default QUIC parameters is designed for datacentres and like stream_window_size had to be toned down to 1MB, the overall max_windows_size needs to be tamed for the home usage

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `21:47:06` **janeytheterrible** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> I kinda have not aimed at data centers and working well for huge corporate networks 😉 Sorta my thing... [truncated]

Here is an exchange where testing showed they had to reduce the window size due to frame blocking  to get better results.  Note a frame is a window_sized data block.  When set to 10MB Max (initial) then router buffers overflow with just a few chunks from the one machine (multiple nodes here) https://www.mail-archive.com/quic%40ietf.org/msg03789.html

And here, while only one QUIC on a machine (we have one for each node, so multiply the issues and therein is the problems of router buffer overflow)  https://docs.google.com/document/d/1F2YfdDXKpy20WVKJueEf4abn_LVZHhMUMS5gX6Pgjl4/mobilebasic

Even Google sets their default initial window sizes to very small values
```
Default values

Google’s servers default to enable auto-tuning for  receive buffers, with the following initial window size settings:

   CFCW: 49152 // 48 KB
  SFCW: 32768 // 32 KB
```

And the QUIC documents says to set that value for your application.  Remember with multiple nodes (independent QUICs) then buffer size in the potato ISP routers are a constraint that QUIC QUIC does not know about and has to learn for each new connection (chunk/node)
```
There is a maximum flow control receive window size which is chosen independently by each endpoint. An endpoint should base this decision on available resources - if you are not constrained by memory then set a large window of 100 Mb for example, whereas a busy server may set a window of 64 Kb. ```

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1315677640581054464/1475247557738234017)

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `10:02:00` **dirvine.** said:

To me, we need to get to a position where nodes are adaptive and can actually self-configure. There is no real "golden set" of configurations; networking is a nightmare, which is why there are so many settings, yet none of them suit everybody. While advanced users in the community might not mind tweaking things, that isn't the goal here. The goal should be "click, install, and work," so nodes must become much more adaptive.

Where we do have issues—which QUIC tries to address—is when you need negotiated protocol settings. There are quite a lot of them, and that's another angle to consider. It is a bit like a spaceship: if someone suggests taking one part out, it feels dangerous.

I believe the network will eventually evolve into an adaptive mechanism where nodes self-configure over time. That is the ultimate goal, because otherwise, networking is simply too hard. People will always want the specific configuration they think suits them, but the amount of parameters is staggering. Since personal networks change constantly, leaning toward adaptive nodes is a key component.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1315677640581054464/1475794890028748801)

---

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `10:12:56` **dirvine.** said:

I feel we should move away from this "node runner" concept, which is probably alarming for some people. The key really is that these nodes should run on everyone's computer without needing lots of configuration, and they certainly should not be affecting the computer or the network adversely.

Basically, they should be an almost invisible component of the applications people are running. That invisible component should allow them to share the resources of their machine with people who have fewer resources, who may need to use tokens to store data instead of buying new machines.

The winning component is that even if your machine blows up or catches fire, your data is still okay if you are storing it on the network.

I feel like we are missing the target with the amount of work being done for node runners. When it becomes a "node runner" conversation, it all becomes about money:
1. How much am I getting?
2. How much can I earn?
3. How many of these things can I get to make more money?

While that is fascinating in some ways, I think it means we've missed the target slightly. It should be about secure access for everyone. Everyone should be able to participate fully in the network, and the "node runner" thing has just never felt very good to me.

It has been great to test nodes, but that is not the direction. The direction is that these nodes should be really beneficial to everybody. People should have a clear understanding that their data is secure—not only from people reading it, but from the raw hardware melting down.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1315677640581054464/1475797642482159636)

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `10:44:56` **dirvine.** said:

This is another advantage of AI. We're moving into a different world where these things will be on 24/7. But even without it being on 24/7, if the network is adaptive enough, that shouldn't matter.

Autonomi 2, for instance, has a neural network and LSTM (Long Short-Term Memory), which allows it to:
1. Predict when particular computers are off and on
2. Work out churn prediction

This is what I mean about being adaptive: the network has to be adaptive, and not only in the networking core, if you know what I mean.

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `14:07:48` **traktion0_20257** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> I feel we should move away from this "node runner" concept, which is probably alarming for some peop... [truncated]

Personally, I think all flavours of node running should be tolerated. I suspect there will always be a mix of flavours too, unless there is code to be hostile against certain uses (which may be tough in itself).

For example, I may want a 'light' app which doesn't do node duties. A simple, thin client app. Likewise, I may want a 'heavy' app, which runs a node too, as it is long running and I don't want to think about node setup. I may want to run the 'light' version on my phone, but then run some nodes on spare, old, hardware at home to earn tokens to fund the 'light' app operation.

So, it feels like a choice thing. Maybe the default should be the simplest, but power users will always tinker. There may also be a question of long running nodes, which need 24/7 access, to avoid heavy churn, improve network performance, etc. It feels like there nedes to be a balance across these different needs of users and the network.

 ### Commits where max_stream_data (or equivalent QUIC receive window behavior) changed

 quic_config.max_stream_data = <env parsed u32>.
 - 473b92019 (2025-06-12)
 File move: ant-networking/src/transport.rs → ant-node/src/networking/transport.rs
 Change: Code moved (behavior preserved).
 - 7ec45124a (2025-11-14)
 File: autonomi/src/networking/driver/mod.rs
 Change: Client set hardcoded:
 quic_config.max_stream_data = 1024 * 1024 (1MB).

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `21:34:46` **janeytheterrible** replied to dirvine.:

> *dirvine. said:*
> This is another advantage of AI. We're moving into a different world where these things will be on 2... [truncated]

FYI in case you had not seen this in QUIC before

Did you know about QUIC doing some of this work taking in suggestions for adapting.  You could have your adaptive system do its magic of analysing conditions and so on and that help QUIC do its job.

_"I believe the network will eventually evolve into an adaptive mechanism where nodes self-configure over time. "_

One of the things that QUIC allows it to be told, amongst others, is a initial_window_size which helps.  Since QUIC on a home system will always see a 1Gbps network connection, never blocked since its UDP, it needs helps to not cause buffer overflows in the router.  8MB buffers are a pain.

So setting initial_window_size based on your adaptive system will allow each node and its copy of QUIC to be helped.  I would say the response time to the first messages to the receiving node can set a base line for lag to that receiving node and then your adaptive system can monitor retry requests to be able to tailor things.

Its one of the settings for this purpose.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1315677640581054464/1475969230259224636)
